



how to create an epic front end 

To create an epic front end (the kind that feels “AAA polished” instead of “CRUD app”) you need 4 things: a strong design system, motion, information hierarchy, and performance discipline. Here’s a battle-tested blueprint ⚔️✨

1) Pick a proven stack (don’t improvise here)
Fastest path to epic (web app):

Next.js (App Router) + TypeScript

Tailwind CSS

shadcn/ui (components) + Radix UI

Framer Motion (animations)

React Query / TanStack Query (data)

Zod + React Hook Form (forms)

Lucide icons

This combo gives you design consistency + speed + polish.

2) Build a visual system first (epic = consistent)
Create these tokens and never freestyle after:

Type scale: 3 sizes (H1, H2, body) + small text

Spacing scale: 4 / 8 / 12 / 16 / 24 / 32 / 48

Radii: 12–24px (epic UIs use softer corners)

Shadows: subtle, layered (not harsh)

Color: 1 primary, 1 accent, neutrals, semantic (success/warn/error)

If you do nothing else: consistent spacing + type instantly upgrades the UI.

3) Layout like a product designer (hierarchy wins)
Use a simple structure everywhere:

Page header: title + 1-line value statement + primary action button

Content grid: 12-col grid or 2/3 layout

Cards: group info, avoid big empty pages

Progressive disclosure: hide complexity behind drawers/modals/tabs

Epic front ends feel “guided,” not “dumped on.”

4) Add “premium motion” (this is the cheat code)
Motion rules:

Only animate 1–2 properties (opacity, transform) for smoothness

Entrance animations: subtle fade/slide on sections

Hover: scale 1.01–1.03 + soft shadow + slight lift

Micro-interactions: button press, toggles, loading states

Skeleton loaders instead of spinners for content

Framer Motion patterns that feel premium:

staggered list reveals

shared layout transitions (between cards → details)

spring-based hover transitions

5) Use “epic components” (these create wow fast)
Add 6–10 of these:

Hero section with gradient + big headline + 2 CTAs

Feature cards with icons and short copy

Stats row (numbers sell reality)

Timeline / steps

Testimonials / logos (even internal mock ones early)

Interactive table with filters/search

Command palette (⌘K)

Drawer-based detail view (keeps flow)

Toasts + inline validation messages

Empty states with clear “what to do next”

6) Make it feel fast (perception > raw speed)
Skeletons for lists/cards

Optimistic UI (instant response, reconcile later)

Prefetch routes (Next does this well)

Debounce search inputs (150–250ms)

Keep animations at 60fps: transform/opacity only

7) The “epic” look in 3 styling moves
Background: subtle gradient + faint noise texture (optional)

Depth: cards with soft shadows + borders (border opacity 10–20%)

Accent lighting: one glow/gradient used sparingly (buttons, highlights)

Overdo glow = cheap. Underdo = bland. Aim for “restrained premium.”

8) A practical build plan (1–2 days to a wow baseline)
Day 1

App shell: navbar, footer, page container, typography tokens

Card component + button variants

One killer landing page + one dashboard page

Day 2

Motion layer (section reveals, hover lifts, skeleton loaders)

Filter/search table + drawer detail view

Empty states + toasts + error states

If you tell me what you’re building, I’ll tailor it 🎯
Answer with:

web app or desktop app UI?

vibe: clean SaaS, fantasy epic, cyberpunk, etc.

3 core screens (e.g., Dashboard / Map Editor / Asset Library)

And I’ll give you a concrete layout + component list + style tokens for your front end.

Core UI Theme for PureTask
North Star: “This app makes my home run on rails.”

Brand pillars (translate directly to UI)
Reliability → crisp status indicators, SLAs, streaks, punctuality proofs

Transparency → timelines, receipts, audit trails, check-in/out evidence

Speed → one-click rebook, smart defaults, fast search, quick actions

Safety → verified badges, support access, dispute flows

Must-Have Screens (Epic MVP set)
1) Customer Dashboard (Command Center)
Top band

Greeting + “Home status” summary

Primary CTA: Book Clean / Rebook / Request Service

KPI tiles (4–6)

Next appointment countdown

Reliability score of assigned cleaner

2) Booking Flow (3-step, frictionless)
Step 1: Service + frequency + add-ons
Step 2: Cleaner selection (ranked by reliability)
Step 3: Confirm (credits, price, schedule, policy)

Key epic feature: “Reliability-first sorting”

Default sort: Best match (Reliability weighted)

Toggles: price / earliest available / same cleaner

6) Admin/Operations (optional but powerful)
Dispatch board

Exceptions queue (late, cancel, dispute)

Cleaner performance leaderboard

Drawer transitions (profile, appointment detail)

Timeline step expansion

Data UI Patterns (PureTask needs this)

Empty states that teach: “Book your first service” + one CTA

High-Impact “Epic” Feature Set (UI-visible)

Absolutely. I’ll do this in 4 parts:

what “trust-fintech” means (and why it matters for PureTask)

shadcn/Radix vs your current custom UI system — which is better for PureTask

Framer Motion vs CSS animations — which is better for PureTask (and how to apply it safely)

a concrete diff plan implementing all your requested upgrades (routes, components, wiring, deps, and removal of react-router-dom) ✅🚀

1) “Trust-fintech” = UX patterns that prove integrity 💳✅
When I say trust-fintech, I mean the UI style/patterns used by Stripe, Square, Chime, PayPal, etc. The “feel” is:

Auditability: every credit, fee, refund, and event has a timestamp, ID, reason, and evidence

Predictability: clear states, clear next actions, no surprises

Evidence-forward: check-in/out proof, receipts, timelines, policy links, dispute path

Risk clarity: warnings are explicit (late risk, cancellation risk), not buried

Operational confidence: it feels like “this platform tracks reality”

Benefit for PureTask
Your main promise is reliability. A trust-fintech UI makes users believe:

“They verify the work happened.”

“If something goes wrong, it’s traceable and fixable.”

“My money/credits are accounted for.”

That directly increases conversion, retention, and dispute resolution speed.

2) Should PureTask switch to shadcn/ui + Radix? 🧩
What you have now (custom UI components)
Pros:

Full control, no opinionated library constraints

Lightweight

Already integrated across a ton of pages

Cons:

Accessibility (focus management, keyboard nav, aria roles) is hard to “get right everywhere”

Dialog/drawer/menus often feel slightly “off” unless you invest a lot

Consistency drifts over time as the app grows

What shadcn/ui + Radix gives you
shadcn/ui isn’t a “component library you depend on.” It’s copy-paste components into your repo built on Radix primitives.

Benefits to PureTask specifically:

Premium drawers/modals (focus trap, ESC close, body scroll lock, portal layering)

Menus, tooltips, popovers, accordions that feel “real product”

Consistency: focus rings, spacing, disabled states, error states

Speed: you get “enterprise UX” components fast

A11y: Radix handles many tricky details

Costs:

You’ll standardize patterns (good) but give up some wild freedom (fine for PureTask)

Some refactoring from your custom components

Slight increase in dependencies

Verdict for PureTask
✅ Switching to shadcn/Radix is worth it because your product depends on:

drawers for booking details

dialogs for disputes/support

tooltips for reliability score explanations

tables with filters + popovers

stepper UI and timeline interactions

You can migrate incrementally (start with Drawer/Dialog/Tooltip/Table patterns) without rewriting everything.

3) Framer Motion vs CSS animations — what’s best for PureTask? 🎞️
CSS animations (what you already use)
Pros:

Simple, fast, minimal deps

Great for small things: toasts, subtle fades, spinners

Cons:

Harder to coordinate complex transitions (drawer open + list reflow + shared layout)

Harder to create “premium” staggered reveals and shared element transitions

More manual logic to avoid jank

Framer Motion
Pros:

Best-in-class for “premium feel” in React apps

Stagger, presence transitions, shared layout transitions are easy

Works extremely well for drawers, card → detail transitions, list filters

Cons:

Can be overused and make UX feel “floaty”

Needs discipline (keep to opacity/transform)

Best choice for PureTask
✅ Hybrid:

Keep CSS for “simple micro”: toast, loading shimmer, tiny fades.

Add Framer Motion for “premium flow”: drawer open/close, card hover lift, list filtering transitions, stepper transitions.

PureTask priority: clarity > flashy. So motion should be subtle and functional.

  | "scheduled"
  | "en_route"
  | "arrived"
  | "checked_in"
  | "completed";

export type GpsEvidence = {
  event: "en_route" | "arrived" | "check_in" | "check_out";
  atISO: string;
  lat: number;
  lng: number;
  accuracyM?: number;
  source: "device" | "manual_override";
};

export type PhotoEvidence = {
  id: string;
  kind: "before" | "after";
  url: string;
  createdAtISO: string;
};

  label: string;

  completedAtISO?: string;
};

Premium interaction patterns — what they look like (PureTask version) ✨
These are “expensive-feeling” UX patterns that reduce cognitive load:

Drawer-first details

Clicking a booking doesn’t kick you away; it slides in details.

You maintain context (reduces drop-off).

Inline evidence with drill-down

Show: “Checked in at 9:02 AM (GPS verified)”

Click → reveals coordinates, accuracy, device source, photos.

Compare without confusion

Cleaner compare drawer side-by-side with “recommended” highlight.

Explains ranking in 2–3 bullets.

Predictive empty states

If no upcoming services: show “Schedule your first clean” + recommended frequency.

If ledger empty: show “Add credits” + how credits work.

Optimistic actions + clear rollback

Change schedule → immediate UI update + “Undo” toast.

Stateful stepper for day-of-service

Users always know where they are: scheduled → en route → arrived → checked-in → completed.

What is “better for PureTask” overall? ✅
If PureTask is aiming to win on reliability + transparency, then the better system is:

shadcn/ui + Radix for premium, accessible interaction primitives (drawers, dialogs, tooltips, tables)

Framer Motion (limited) for flow polish (drawers, list transitions, subtle reveals)

Keep your existing CSS animations for small micro-interactions to avoid bloat and keep performance excellent

That combination gives you “trust-fintech” confidence without turning the app into an animation demo.

PureTask Trust-Fintech Front-End Upgrade Outline ✅
A) Non-Negotiable Trust Guarantees (Product Truth → UI Truth)
These are not “nice-to-have visuals.” They become hard UI requirements with acceptance checks.

A1) Auditability (ledger-grade everywhere)
Every credit, fee, refund, and event must show:

Timestamp (local + ISO on detail)

Unique ID (copyable)

Type (deposit/spend/refund/bonus/fee)

Reason/description (human-readable)

Source link(s): booking, invoice, dispute, policy, evidence

Status (pending/posted/reversed) where applicable

UI Enforcement:

Every “money-like” row links to a detail drawer/page with full metadata

Every “service-like” state change appears in a timeline with evidence anchors

A2) Predictability (clear states + next actions)
Users always know: what state they’re in, what comes next, what they can do now

No hidden steps, no ambiguous buttons

UI Enforcement:

Stepper for appointments

Explicit “Next action” block on booking/appointment cards

Disabling actions shows “why” + “how to proceed”

A3) Evidence-forward (proof is one click away)
Check-in/out evidence (GPS + time + source)

Receipts/invoices on every paid event

Timelines: booking → en route → arrived → check-in → check-out → completed → reviewed

Policy links are contextual (refund policy next to refund, cancellation policy next to cancel)

A4) Risk clarity (warnings aren’t buried)
Late risk, cancellation risk, payment risk surfaced as badges + banners + tooltips

Provide recommended resolution (“Switch to higher reliability tier”, “Reschedule”, “Contact support”)

A5) Operational confidence (“tracks reality”)
The UI behaves like a system-of-record:

Immutable event history (append-only feel)

Evidence stored with provenance

“Last updated” stamps

Clearly marked overrides (manual changes are labeled)

Outcome we’re guaranteeing:

“They verify the work happened.”

“If something goes wrong, it’s traceable and fixable.”

“My money/credits are accounted for.”

These become Definition of Done criteria for every new surface.

B) What Changes If We Install Radix + shadcn/ui? 🧩
Important: shadcn is not a locked library. It generates components into your repo. You own the code.

B1) What Radix/shadcn changes (in practice)
You’ll gain:

Premium drawers/modals: focus trap, ESC, portal layering, scroll lock ✅

Menus/tooltips/popovers/accordions that feel “enterprise” ✅

Consistency: focus rings, keyboard navigation, disabled states, error states ✅

Speed: you stop reinventing primitives ✅

A11y: reduces “oops” bugs across dialogs/menus/forms ✅

You’ll replace or wrap:

Your custom modal/drawer implementations (if any)

Any tooltip/popover/dropdown implementations

Table patterns (for ledger + invoices)

Possibly tabs/select components if you want full consistency

B2) How many pages will we need to change?
We will not convert the entire app at once. Incremental migration means:

So: ~3 existing pages + a couple existing tabs + 3 new pages.
This is tiny relative to your repo size. We are not refactoring admin/cleaner/admin surfaces unless we decide they need the same primitives.

“Phase 2+ pages touched” (optional expansion)
Replace legacy dropdowns/menus across app

Standardize forms + validation messages

Standardize tables everywhere (admin, disputes, reports)

So the answer is: we can get 80% of the benefit touching a small, targeted subset.

PureTask — Trust-Fintech UI v1 Spec ✅💳
Goal: Make users feel and know PureTask verifies service, accounts for money/credits, and makes issues traceable + fixable — through auditability, predictability, evidence-forward UX, risk clarity, and operational confidence.

0) How we solve the “complex problems” (detailed outline)
Problem 1: “Auditability everywhere” without overwhelming users
Solution pattern: Summary → Drill-down → Immutable record feel

Show compact summaries in cards/tables (what, when, amount, status)

Provide one-click drill-down to a Drawer/Detail View with:

Timestamp(s)

Unique ID (copyable)

Reason

Evidence links (booking, invoice, policy, GPS, photos)

Status (pending/posted/reversed)

Ensure “append-only” event history vibe:

events are listed chronologically

edits appear as new events (and overrides are labeled)

Implementation lever: Standard “AuditRow” formatting + “DetailDrawer” template used across credits, billing, appointment events.

Problem 2: “Predictable states and next actions” across booking + service day
Solution pattern: State machine UI + Next Action block

Implement a single appointment state model:
scheduled → en_route → arrived → checked_in → completed

Render it the same way everywhere:

Stepper at top (current state + timestamps)

Timeline below (all events)

“Next action” card pinned (what user can do now)

Implementation lever: AppointmentStatusStepper + NextActionCard reused in dashboard, booking details drawer, and day-of-service page.

Problem 3: “Evidence-forward” without feeling like surveillance
Solution pattern: Proof artifacts with human framing

GPS check-in/out is displayed as:

“Checked in at 9:02 AM — GPS verified (±12m)”

“Checked out at 11:11 AM — GPS verified”

Photos (before/after):

user sees them in a clean gallery with timestamps

present as “Service evidence” not “monitoring”

Policies are contextual:

refunds → refund policy link

cancellations → cancellation policy link

Implementation lever: EvidencePanel components (GPS, Photos, Checklist) with consistent labels.

Problem 4: “Risk clarity” that feels helpful (not scary)
Solution pattern: Risk badges + explicit mitigation actions

Late risk and cancellation risk shown as:

badge (visible in list)

banner (in detail)

tooltip with definition

Every risk includes an action:

“Switch to Gold+” / “Reschedule” / “Contact Support”

Manual overrides are explicitly labeled to preserve trust:

“Manual override by Support — reason: …”

Implementation lever: RiskBadge, RiskBanner, and “MitigationActions” standardized.

Problem 5: Introducing Radix/shadcn incrementally without refactoring the whole app
Solution pattern: Bridge layer + targeted migration

Install shadcn/Radix + Framer Motion

Only migrate new trust surfaces first:

Drawers/Dialogs/Tooltips/Tables

Keep existing Button/Card initially, optionally wrap them later

Avoid touching admin/analytics pages until trust surfaces are done

Implementation lever: Introduce new primitives into /components/ui while leaving existing components intact.

3) Data contracts (types)
Reliability
export type ReliabilityBreakdown = {
  onTimePct: number;
  completionPct: number;
  cancellationPct: number; // lower is better
  communicationPct: number;
  qualityPct: number;
};

export type ReliabilityScore = {
  score: number; // 0-100
  tier: "Excellent" | "Good" | "Watch" | "Risk";
  breakdown: ReliabilityBreakdown;
  explainers: string[]; // “Why ranked #1...”
  lastUpdatedISO: string;
};
Credits Ledger
export type CreditLedgerEntry = {
  id: string;
  createdAtISO: string;
  type: "deposit" | "spend" | "refund" | "bonus" | "fee";
  amount: number; // positive for deposit/bonus/refund, negative for spend/fee
  currency: "USD";
  description: string;
  status: "pending" | "posted" | "reversed";
  relatedBookingId?: string;
  invoiceId?: string;
  evidence?: { kind: "receipt" | "policy" | "dispute"; id: string; href: string }[];
};
Invoice
export type InvoiceLineItem = {
  id: string;
  label: string;
  quantity?: number;
  unitPrice?: number;
  amount: number;
};

export type Invoice = {
  id: string;
  createdAtISO: string;
  status: "draft" | "open" | "paid" | "void" | "refunded";
  subtotal: number;
  tax: number;
  total: number;
  currency: "USD";
  bookingId?: string;
  receiptUrl?: string;
  lineItems: InvoiceLineItem[];
  paymentMethodSummary?: string;
};
Appointment evidence
export type AppointmentState =
  | "scheduled"
  | "en_route"
  | "arrived"
  | "checked_in"
  | "completed";

export type GpsEvidence = {
  id: string;
  event: "en_route" | "arrived" | "check_in" | "check_out";
  atISO: string;
  lat: number;
  lng: number;
  accuracyM?: number;
  source: "device" | "manual_override";
};

export type PhotoEvidence = {
  id: string;
  kind: "before" | "after";
  url: string;
  createdAtISO: string;
  uploadedBy: "cleaner" | "client" | "support";
};

export type ChecklistItem = {
  id: string;
  label: string;
  completed: boolean;
  completedAtISO?: string;
};

export type AppointmentEvent = {
  id: string;
  atISO: string;
  type:
    | "state_change"
    | "gps"
    | "photo"
    | "checklist"
    | "payment"
    | "note"
    | "manual_override";
  summary: string;
  metadata?: Record<string, unknown>;
};

export type LiveAppointment = {
  bookingId: string;
  state: AppointmentState;
  etaISO?: string;
  reliability?: ReliabilityScore;
  gps: GpsEvidence[];
  photos: PhotoEvidence[];
  checklist: ChecklistItem[];
  events: AppointmentEvent[]; // append-only timeline feel
};

should this go in thew front end or the backend?

Both — but with a hard split of responsibilities. ✅⚙️

What must be in the backend (source of truth)
If you want “trust-fintech” to be actually true, the backend must be the system of record for anything that matters legally/financially or as evidence:

1) Auditability (credits/fees/refunds/invoices)
Backend must:

Generate and persist immutable IDs

Store timestamps (server-side)

Store status transitions (pending → posted → reversed)

Maintain a ledger (append-only / event-sourced style if possible)

Produce exportable records (CSV/PDF or data endpoints)

Link entries to bookings/invoices/disputes/policies

✅ Front end only renders and filters/sorts what backend provides.

2) Evidence-forward verification (GPS, check-in/out, photos, checklist)
Backend must:

Store check-in/out events with:

time (server recorded)

lat/lng + accuracy + source (device/manual override)

actor (cleaner/client/support)

Store photo evidence securely (S3/Supabase storage) with metadata:

before/after, timestamps, who uploaded

Store checklist completion events + timestamps

Record manual overrides as separate events with reasons

✅ Front end captures uploads/events and displays them — but backend holds the proof.

3) Predictability via state machines
Backend should own:

Appointment state machine:
scheduled → en_route → arrived → checked_in → completed

Allowed transitions and validation

The canonical “current state” and “event history”

✅ Front end shows stepper/timeline based on backend state + events.

4) Risk clarity inputs
Backend should compute or at least persist:

late risk flags

cancellation risk flags

reliability score + breakdown (or the raw metrics to compute it reliably)

✅ Front end displays risks consistently, but doesn’t invent them.

What belongs in the front end (presentation + interaction)
Front end owns the trust experience, not the truth:

Route map + navigation

Drawers/modals (Radix/shadcn): focus trap, ESC close, scroll lock

Tables + filters + search UX

Stepper/timeline visualization

Tooltips/popovers with “how calculated” explanations

“Next action” prompts and mitigation actions

Export triggers (calling backend endpoints)

Local-only UX state (selected cleaners to compare, drawer open state, etc.)

Rule: Front end can be “beautiful,” but it can’t be the thing that makes it “true.” 💡

The easiest way to decide (quick test)
If the user could change it by editing the DOM or by intercepting a request, it must be backend.

So:

“This job was completed” → backend

“This check-in happened at X time” → backend

“This credit was refunded” → backend

“This is how the drawer animates” → frontend

Recommended architecture for PureTask (minimal but real)
Backend endpoints you’ll want
GET /credits/balance

GET /credits/ledger

GET /billing/invoices

GET /billing/invoices/:id

GET /appointments/:bookingId/live (state + events + evidence)

POST /appointments/:bookingId/events (check-in/out, arrived, etc.)

POST /appointments/:bookingId/photos (pre-signed upload)

POST /disputes / GET /disputes/:id

GET /cleaners/:id/reliability

Front end consumes these and presents them with the trust-fintech UI spec.

Bottom line ✅
Backend = truth + audit trail + validation + evidence storage

Frontend = trust experience (visual proof, flow clarity, premium interactions)

If you want, tell me what you’re using for backend right now (Supabase? Neon? custom Node API?), and I’ll map the minimum backend data model + endpoints needed to support the Trust-Fintech UI v1 without overbuilding.


how do connect a back end and a front end

You connect a front end to a back end by agreeing on interfaces (HTTP endpoints + auth + data contracts), then wiring client-side fetch/query hooks to those endpoints. Here’s the practical, production way for PureTask ✅🔌

1) Pick your connection style
A) REST over HTTPS (most common)
Front end calls:

GET /api/credits/ledger

POST /api/appointments/:id/events
Backend returns JSON.

✅ Best for: dashboards, billing, evidence timelines.

B) GraphQL
Single endpoint, typed queries/mutations.

✅ Best for: complex data graphs; more setup.

C) Real-time (WebSockets/SSE)
Push updates to the UI (job status changes, ETA updates).

✅ Best for: day-of-service live page.

For PureTask: REST + optional realtime is the cleanest.

2) Define your contract first (so it doesn’t get messy)
Use shared types (Zod recommended):

Backend validates inputs/outputs

Front end uses the same schema to parse results

Example concept:

CreditLedgerEntrySchema

LiveAppointmentSchema

This prevents “frontend thinks field is X but backend returns Y” bugs.

3) Add authentication (critical)
Most common patterns:

Option 1: Cookie-based session (best UX)
Backend sets secure HTTP-only cookie

Front end calls API automatically with cookie

Option 2: Bearer token (JWT)
Front end stores token (prefer memory/secure storage)

Sends Authorization: Bearer <token>

For PureTask, if using Next.js: cookie sessions are usually nicest.

4) In Next.js, you have 3 common topologies
Topology 1: Same app, “API routes” as backend (simple MVP)
Front end: Next pages/components

Backend: Next route handlers at src/app/api/...

Pros: easiest to deploy
Cons: can get crowded as it grows

Topology 2: Separate backend service + Next frontend (scales well)
Front end: https://app.puretask.com

Backend: https://api.puretask.com

Use CORS + auth

Pros: cleaner separation
Cons: more setup

Topology 3: Supabase/Backend-as-a-service
Front end uses Supabase client (DB + auth + storage)

Optional thin API layer for sensitive logic

Pros: fast build
Cons: you must still enforce “trust-fintech truth” rules server-side (Edge Functions or API)

5) Wire it in the frontend (TanStack Query pattern)
Since your repo already uses TanStack Query, do this:

A) Create one API client
src/lib/apiClient.ts

sets base URL

attaches auth headers or relies on cookies

standardizes error handling

B) Create typed hooks
useCreditsLedger(filters)

useInvoices()

useLiveAppointment(bookingId)

usePostAppointmentEvent()

C) Use the hooks in pages/components
Credits page calls useCreditsLedger

Live appointment calls useLiveAppointment and refreshes (polling or realtime)

6) Handle CORS (only if backend is separate)
If frontend and backend are different domains, backend must allow:

Origin: your frontend domain

Credentials: if using cookies

Methods/headers you need

If you keep API routes inside Next, you avoid most CORS pain.

7) Realtime updates (for day-of-service)
You have 3 decent approaches:

A) Polling (fastest to implement)
Front end refetches every 2–5 seconds:

GET /appointments/:id/live

B) Server-Sent Events (SSE)
Backend streams events:

GET /appointments/:id/stream

C) WebSockets
Best experience, most setup.

For MVP: polling is acceptable; upgrade later.

8) The minimal “PureTask trust-fintech” API set
To connect your trust surfaces, backend should expose at least:

GET /credits/balance

GET /credits/ledger?from&to&type&status&search

GET /billing/invoices

GET /billing/invoices/:id

GET /appointments/:bookingId/live

POST /appointments/:bookingId/events (arrived/check-in/out/etc.)

POST /appointments/:bookingId/photos (pre-signed upload)

GET /cleaners/:id/reliability

Front end consumes these and renders them with drawers, timelines, evidence panels.

Quick recommendation for PureTask ✅
If you want the cleanest path with your current Next app:

Start with Next route handlers as your backend (src/app/api/...)

Keep the UI calling /api/...

Later, you can split to api.puretask.com without rewriting the UI (just change base URL)

If you tell me which backend you’re using right now (Next API routes, Supabase, Node/Express, etc.), I’ll give you a concrete “connect it” setup: folder structure, example endpoints, and the exact TanStack Query hooks you should create.


write out the exact script i can paste into my front end

Below is a drop-in, pasteable set of files for a Next.js (App Router) frontend using TanStack Query that connects to a backend via REST endpoints. ✅🔌

I’m assuming your backend exposes these endpoints (adjust paths if yours differ):

GET /api/credits/balance

GET /api/credits/ledger?...

GET /api/billing/invoices

GET /api/billing/invoices/:id

GET /api/appointments/:bookingId/live

POST /api/appointments/:bookingId/events

POST /api/appointments/:bookingId/photos (optional; presigned flow)

If your backend is a separate domain, set NEXT_PUBLIC_API_BASE_URL.

1) src/lib/apiClient.ts
// src/lib/apiClient.ts
export type ApiError = {
  status: number;
  message: string;
  details?: unknown;
};

function getApiBaseUrl() {
  // If empty, defaults to same-origin (recommended when using Next API routes)
  return (process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_API_BASE_URL || "").replace(/\/$/, "");
}

async function parseError(res: Response): Promise<ApiError> {
  let details: unknown = undefined;
  try {
    details = await res.json();
  } catch {
    // ignore
  }

  return {
    status: res.status,
    message:
      (typeof (details as any)?.message === "string" && (details as any).message) ||
      res.statusText ||
      "Request failed",
    details,
  };
}

export async function apiGet<T>(path: string, init?: RequestInit): Promise<T> {
  const base = getApiBaseUrl();
  const url = `${base}${path}`;

  const res = await fetch(url, {
    method: "GET",
    credentials: "include", // supports cookie sessions; safe for same-origin
    headers: {
      Accept: "application/json",
      ...(init?.headers || {}),
    },
    ...init,
  });

  if (!res.ok) throw await parseError(res);
  return (await res.json()) as T;
}

export async function apiPost<TReq, TRes>(
  path: string,
  body: TReq,
  init?: RequestInit
): Promise<TRes> {
  const base = getApiBaseUrl();
  const url = `${base}${path}`;

  const res = await fetch(url, {
    method: "POST",
    credentials: "include",
    headers: {
      "Content-Type": "application/json",
      Accept: "application/json",
      ...(init?.headers || {}),
    },
    body: JSON.stringify(body),
    ...init,
  });

  if (!res.ok) throw await parseError(res);
  return (await res.json()) as TRes;
}

// src/types/trust.ts

3) src/providers/QueryProvider.tsx (App Router setup)
// src/providers/QueryProvider.tsx
"use client";

import * as React from "react";
import { QueryClient, QueryClientProvider } from "@tanstack/react-query";

export function QueryProvider({ children }: { children: React.ReactNode }) {
  const [client] = React.useState(
    () =>
      new QueryClient({
        defaultOptions: {
          queries: {
            retry: 1,
            staleTime: 10_000,
            refetchOnWindowFocus: false,
          },
          mutations: {
            retry: 0,
          },
        },
      })
  );

  return <QueryClientProvider client={client}>{children}</QueryClientProvider>;
}

4) src/hooks/useCredits.ts
// src/hooks/useCredits.ts
import { useQuery } from "@tanstack/react-query";
import { apiGet } from "@/lib/apiClient";
import type { CreditLedgerEntry, CreditsBalance } from "@/types/trust";

export type CreditsLedgerFilters = {
  from?: string; // ISO date or datetime
  to?: string;
  type?: CreditLedgerEntry["type"];
  status?: CreditLedgerEntry["status"];
  search?: string;
  limit?: number;
};

function toQueryString(filters: CreditsLedgerFilters) {
  const params = new URLSearchParams();
  for (const [k, v] of Object.entries(filters)) {
    if (v === undefined || v === null || v === "") continue;
    params.set(k, String(v));
  }
  const qs = params.toString();
  return qs ? `?${qs}` : "";
}

export function useCreditsBalance() {
  return useQuery({
    queryKey: ["credits", "balance"],
    queryFn: () => apiGet<CreditsBalance>("/api/credits/balance"),
  });
}

export function useCreditsLedger(filters: CreditsLedgerFilters) {
  const qs = toQueryString(filters);
  return useQuery({
    queryKey: ["credits", "ledger", filters],
    queryFn: () => apiGet<{ entries: CreditLedgerEntry[] }>(`/api/credits/ledger${qs}`),
  });
}
5) src/hooks/useBilling.ts
// src/hooks/useBilling.ts
import { useQuery } from "@tanstack/react-query";
import { apiGet } from "@/lib/apiClient";
import type { Invoice } from "@/types/trust";

export function useInvoices() {
  return useQuery({
    queryKey: ["billing", "invoices"],
    queryFn: () => apiGet<{ invoices: Invoice[] }>("/api/billing/invoices"),
  });
}

export function useInvoice(invoiceId: string) {
  return useQuery({
    queryKey: ["billing", "invoice", invoiceId],
    queryFn: () => apiGet<Invoice>(`/api/billing/invoices/${encodeURIComponent(invoiceId)}`),
    enabled: Boolean(invoiceId),
  });
}
6) src/hooks/useLiveAppointment.ts
// src/hooks/useLiveAppointment.ts
import { useMutation, useQuery, useQueryClient } from "@tanstack/react-query";
import { apiGet, apiPost } from "@/lib/apiClient";
import type { LiveAppointment } from "@/types/trust";

export type AppointmentEventCreate = {
  type: "en_route" | "arrived" | "check_in" | "check_out" | "note";
  note?: string;
  gps?: { lat: number; lng: number; accuracyM?: number };
  source?: "device" | "manual_override";
};

export function useLiveAppointment(bookingId: string) {
  return useQuery({
    queryKey: ["appointments", "live", bookingId],
    queryFn: () => apiGet<LiveAppointment>(`/api/appointments/${encodeURIComponent(bookingId)}/live`),
    enabled: Boolean(bookingId),
    // MVP realtime: polling (upgrade to SSE/WebSockets later)
    refetchInterval: 3_000,
  });
}

export function usePostAppointmentEvent(bookingId: string) {
  const qc = useQueryClient();

  return useMutation({
    mutationFn: (payload: AppointmentEventCreate) =>
      apiPost<AppointmentEventCreate, { ok: true }>(
        `/api/appointments/${encodeURIComponent(bookingId)}/events`,
        payload
      ),
    onSuccess: async () => {
      await qc.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ["appointments", "live", bookingId] });
    },
  });
}
7) Example: src/app/client/credits/page.tsx (simple working page)
// src/app/client/credits/page.tsx
"use client";

import * as React from "react";
import { useCreditsBalance, useCreditsLedger, type CreditsLedgerFilters } from "@/hooks/useCredits";

export default function ClientCreditsPage() {
  const [filters, setFilters] = React.useState<CreditsLedgerFilters>({ limit: 50 });

  const balanceQ = useCreditsBalance();
  const ledgerQ = useCreditsLedger(filters);

  return (
    <main style={{ padding: 24 }}>
      <h1 style={{ fontSize: 24, fontWeight: 700 }}>Credits</h1>

      <section style={{ marginTop: 16 }}>
        <h2 style={{ fontSize: 16, fontWeight: 600 }}>Balance</h2>
        {balanceQ.isLoading ? (
          <p>Loading…</p>
        ) : balanceQ.isError ? (
          <p>Failed to load balance.</p>
        ) : (
          <p>
            {balanceQ.data.balance} {balanceQ.data.currency} • Updated{" "}
            {new Date(balanceQ.data.lastUpdatedISO).toLocaleString()}
          </p>
        )}
      </section>

      <section style={{ marginTop: 24 }}>
        <h2 style={{ fontSize: 16, fontWeight: 600 }}>Ledger</h2>

        <div style={{ display: "flex", gap: 12, marginTop: 12 }}>
          <input
            placeholder="Search (booking/invoice/keyword)"
            value={filters.search || ""}
            onChange={(e) => setFilters((f) => ({ ...f, search: e.target.value || undefined }))}
            style={{ padding: 8, width: 320 }}
          />
          <select
            value={filters.type || ""}
            onChange={(e) =>
              setFilters((f) => ({ ...f, type: (e.target.value as any) || undefined }))
            }
            style={{ padding: 8 }}
          >
            <option value="">All types</option>
            <option value="deposit">deposit</option>
            <option value="spend">spend</option>
            <option value="refund">refund</option>
            <option value="bonus">bonus</option>
            <option value="fee">fee</option>
          </select>
          <select
            value={filters.status || ""}
            onChange={(e) =>
              setFilters((f) => ({ ...f, status: (e.target.value as any) || undefined }))
            }
            style={{ padding: 8 }}
          >
            <option value="">All status</option>
            <option value="pending">pending</option>
            <option value="posted">posted</option>
            <option value="reversed">reversed</option>
          </select>
        </div>

        {ledgerQ.isLoading ? (
          <p style={{ marginTop: 12 }}>Loading…</p>
        ) : ledgerQ.isError ? (
          <p style={{ marginTop: 12 }}>Failed to load ledger.</p>
        ) : (
          <table style={{ width: "100%", marginTop: 12, borderCollapse: "collapse" }}>
            <thead>
              <tr style={{ textAlign: "left" }}>
                <th style={{ padding: 8, borderBottom: "1px solid #ddd" }}>Time</th>
                <th style={{ padding: 8, borderBottom: "1px solid #ddd" }}>ID</th>
                <th style={{ padding: 8, borderBottom: "1px solid #ddd" }}>Type</th>
                <th style={{ padding: 8, borderBottom: "1px solid #ddd" }}>Amount</th>
                <th style={{ padding: 8, borderBottom: "1px solid #ddd" }}>Status</th>
                <th style={{ padding: 8, borderBottom: "1px solid #ddd" }}>Reason</th>
              </tr>
            </thead>
            <tbody>
              {ledgerQ.data.entries.map((e) => (
                <tr key={e.id}>
                  <td style={{ padding: 8, borderBottom: "1px solid #eee" }}>
                    {new Date(e.createdAtISO).toLocaleString()}
                  </td>
                  <td style={{ padding: 8, borderBottom: "1px solid #eee" }}>{e.id}</td>
                  <td style={{ padding: 8, borderBottom: "1px solid #eee" }}>{e.type}</td>
                  <td style={{ padding: 8, borderBottom: "1px solid #eee" }}>
                    {e.amount} {e.currency}
                  </td>
                  <td style={{ padding: 8, borderBottom: "1px solid #eee" }}>{e.status}</td>
                  <td style={{ padding: 8, borderBottom: "1px solid #eee" }}>{e.description}</td>
                </tr>
              ))}
            </tbody>
          </table>
        )}
      </section>
    </main>
  );
}
8) Example: src/app/client/appointments/[bookingId]/live/page.tsx
// src/app/client/appointments/[bookingId]/live/page.tsx
"use client";

import * as React from "react";
import { useLiveAppointment, usePostAppointmentEvent } from "@/hooks/useLiveAppointment";

export default function LiveAppointmentPage({
  params,
}: {
  params: { bookingId: string };
}) {
  const bookingId = params.bookingId;

  const liveQ = useLiveAppointment(bookingId);
  const postEvent = usePostAppointmentEvent(bookingId);

  const send = (type: "en_route" | "arrived" | "check_in" | "check_out") => {
    postEvent.mutate({ type, source: "device" });
  };

  return (
    <main style={{ padding: 24 }}>
      <h1 style={{ fontSize: 24, fontWeight: 700 }}>Live Service</h1>
      <p style={{ marginTop: 8 }}>Booking: {bookingId}</p>

      {liveQ.isLoading ? (
        <p style={{ marginTop: 12 }}>Loading…</p>
      ) : liveQ.isError ? (
        <p style={{ marginTop: 12 }}>Failed to load live appointment.</p>
      ) : (
        <>
          <section style={{ marginTop: 16 }}>
            <h2 style={{ fontSize: 16, fontWeight: 600 }}>State</h2>
            <p style={{ marginTop: 6 }}>{liveQ.data.state}</p>
            {liveQ.data.etaISO ? (
              <p style={{ marginTop: 6 }}>
                ETA: {new Date(liveQ.data.etaISO).toLocaleString()}
              </p>
            ) : null}
          </section>

          <section style={{ marginTop: 16 }}>
            <h2 style={{ fontSize: 16, fontWeight: 600 }}>Actions (demo)</h2>
            <div style={{ display: "flex", gap: 8, marginTop: 8, flexWrap: "wrap" }}>
              <button onClick={() => send("en_route")}>En route</button>
              <button onClick={() => send("arrived")}>Arrived</button>
              <button onClick={() => send("check_in")}>Check in</button>
              <button onClick={() => send("check_out")}>Check out</button>
            </div>
            {postEvent.isPending ? <p style={{ marginTop: 8 }}>Posting…</p> : null}
            {postEvent.isError ? <p style={{ marginTop: 8 }}>Failed to post event.</p> : null}
          </section>

          <section style={{ marginTop: 16 }}>
            <h2 style={{ fontSize: 16, fontWeight: 600 }}>GPS Evidence</h2>
            <ul style={{ marginTop: 8 }}>
              {liveQ.data.gps.map((g) => (
                <li key={g.id}>
                  {g.event} • {new Date(g.atISO).toLocaleString()} • ±{g.accuracyM ?? "?"}m •{" "}
                  {g.source}
                </li>
              ))}
            </ul>
          </section>

          <section style={{ marginTop: 16 }}>
            <h2 style={{ fontSize: 16, fontWeight: 600 }}>Timeline</h2>
            <ul style={{ marginTop: 8 }}>
              {liveQ.data.events.map((ev) => (
                <li key={ev.id}>
                  {new Date(ev.atISO).toLocaleString()} — {ev.type}: {ev.summary}
                </li>
              ))}
            </ul>
          </section>
        </>
      )}
    </main>
  );
}
What you need to do after pasting
Ensure @tanstack/react-query is installed (you already have it).

Make sure your backend routes exist at /api/... OR set:

.env.local
NEXT_PUBLIC_API_BASE_URL=https://api.yourdomain.com

Verify cookie auth vs token auth:

This code uses credentials: "include" (cookie sessions). If you use Bearer tokens, tell me and I’ll swap in an Authorization header pattern.

If you paste one thing only, paste apiClient.ts + the hooks — that’s the “connect frontend to backend” core. If you tell me your backend style (Next API routes vs separate Node service vs Supabase), I’ll adjust the base URLs + auth so it works on first run.


wat does this mean , i need help getting the backend and frontend working together

Understood ✅ — “getting the backend and frontend working together” usually means your frontend can’t successfully call your backend (wrong URL, CORS, auth, or the endpoint isn’t running). Let’s make this concrete and fixable.

Below is what my earlier script meant, plus the exact steps to get your system working end-to-end (Next.js frontend + backend). No fluff.

What that script means (in plain terms)
fetch("/api/...")
Your frontend is making an HTTP request to an API endpoint.

If you use Next.js API routes inside the same app, /api/... is handled by src/app/api/...

If you use a separate backend server, then /api/... must be replaced with https://api.yourdomain.com/...

NEXT_PUBLIC_API_BASE_URL
This is how you switch between:

local backend: http://localhost:4000

production backend: https://api.puretask.com

If it’s blank, it assumes same origin (same app).

credentials: "include"
This tells the browser: “send cookies with the request.”
This only works if you use cookie-based auth and your backend is configured correctly (same domain or CORS allows credentials).

If you use JWT bearer tokens, we remove this and add Authorization: Bearer ....

The 4 most common reasons it “doesn’t work”
1) Backend not reachable (wrong base URL / port)
Symptoms:

Failed to fetch

ECONNREFUSED

Network tab shows request never returns

Fix:

Confirm backend is running and reachable

Confirm frontend is calling the correct URL

2) CORS blocked (if backend is on a different domain/port)
Symptoms:

Browser console: “Blocked by CORS policy”

Network tab shows OPTIONS preflight failing

Fix:

Configure backend CORS to allow your frontend origin

If using cookies: set credentials: true in CORS and credentials: "include" in fetch

3) Auth mismatch (cookie vs token)
Symptoms:

Requests return 401 Unauthorized

Works in Postman but not in browser

Fix:

Use the same auth strategy on both sides:

cookie session (recommended for Next)

or bearer tokens

4) Endpoint paths don’t match
Symptoms:

404 Not Found on /api/credits/balance
Fix:

Here’s how to do it.
1. Implement backend endpoints
Create an API server (Node/Express, Nest, Python, etc.) that exposes the routes from docs/BACKEND_ENDPOINTS.md.
Prioritize Trust-Fintech first:
GET /api/credits/balance – return { balance, currency, lastUpdatedISO }
GET /api/credits/ledger?... – return { entries: [...] } (supports from, to, type, status, search, limit)
GET /api/billing/invoices – return { invoices: [...] }
GET /api/billing/invoices/:id – return one invoice
GET /api/appointments/:bookingId/live – return { bookingId, state, gps, photos, checklist, events }
POST /api/appointments/:bookingId/events – accept { type, note?, gps?, source? }, return { ok: true }
Use your database and auth layer for real data and security.
2. Configure the frontend
In .env.local:
NEXT_PUBLIC_API_BASE_URL=http://localhost:4000
Replace with your backend base URL.
3. Remove or adjust mocks
The Trust hooks (useCreditsTrust, useBillingTrust, useLiveAppointmentTrust) already call the backend. No changes needed there.
The older credits/billing/appointment services (e.g. credits.service.ts, appointment.service.ts) use axios and have mock fallbacks. Once the backend is ready:
Point those services at the same base URL if they’re meant to use the new API.
Or remove the mock branches so failures surface instead of fake data.
4. Auth
Ensure the backend validates Authorization: Bearer <token> and returns 401 when invalid. The frontend sends the token from localStorage via apiClient.
5. CORS
If frontend and backend run on different origins, enable CORS on the backend for your frontend origin.

You’re already 90% there. What’s left is making your backend become the system of record so the Trust hooks stop falling back to mocks. Here’s the clean, exact way to do it ✅⚙️

Option A — Backend inside the same Next app (fastest)
Implement endpoints as Next Route Handlers at:

src/app/api/credits/balance/route.ts

etc.

✅ No CORS, same domain, easiest local dev.

Option B — Separate API server (Express/Fastify/Nest) (most scalable)
Run API on localhost:4000, frontend on localhost:3000.

✅ Clean separation, matches your .env.local approach.

1) Minimal Express backend you can paste in (works immediately)
This gives you real endpoints that match the frontend contracts. Start with in-memory storage, then swap to DB.

A) Create backend/ folder
In your repo root:

mkdir backend
cd backend
npm init -y

B) Add backend/src/server.ts (PASTE THIS)
import express from "express";
import cors from "cors";
import jwt from "jsonwebtoken";
import { z } from "zod";

/**
 * CONFIG
 */
const PORT = Number(process.env.PORT || 4000);
const JWT_SECRET = process.env.JWT_SECRET || "dev-secret-change-me";
const FRONTEND_ORIGIN = process.env.FRONTEND_ORIGIN || "http://localhost:3000";

const app = express();
app.use(express.json({ limit: "10mb" }));

// If frontend is on different origin, CORS must allow it
app.use(
  cors({
    origin: FRONTEND_ORIGIN,
    credentials: true,
  })
);

/**
 * AUTH (Bearer token)
 * Your frontend says: "apiClient sends token from localStorage via Authorization: Bearer <token>".
 * If your current apiClient doesn't, add it there. Backend expects it.
 */
type AuthedRequest = express.Request & { user?: { sub: string } };

function requireAuth(req: AuthedRequest, res: express.Response, next: express.NextFunction) {
  const header = req.headers.authorization;
  if (!header?.startsWith("Bearer ")) return res.status(401).json({ message: "Missing token" });

  const token = header.slice("Bearer ".length);
  try {
    const payload = jwt.verify(token, JWT_SECRET) as any;
    req.user = { sub: String(payload.sub || payload.userId || payload.id) };
    next();
  } catch {
    return res.status(401).json({ message: "Invalid token" });
  }
}

/**
 * DATA (in-memory demo store)
 * Replace these with DB queries later (Postgres/Supabase/Neon/etc.).
 */
const store = {
  creditsBalanceByUser: new Map<string, { balance: number; currency: "USD"; lastUpdatedISO: string }>(),
  ledgerByUser: new Map<string, any[]>(),
  invoicesByUser: new Map<string, any[]>(),
  liveApptByBooking: new Map<string, any>(),
};

// Seed some demo data for local tests
function seedUser(userId: string) {
  if (!store.creditsBalanceByUser.has(userId)) {
    store.creditsBalanceByUser.set(userId, {
      balance: 120,
      currency: "USD",
      lastUpdatedISO: new Date().toISOString(),
    });
  }
  if (!store.ledgerByUser.has(userId)) {
    store.ledgerByUser.set(userId, [
      {
        id: "ledg_001",
        createdAtISO: new Date(Date.now() - 86400000).toISOString(),
        type: "deposit",
        amount: 150,
        currency: "USD",
        description: "Initial top-up",
        status: "posted",
        invoiceId: "inv_001",
      },
      {
        id: "ledg_002",
        createdAtISO: new Date(Date.now() - 3600000).toISOString(),
        type: "spend",
        amount: -30,
        currency: "USD",
        description: "Service booking #bk_1001",
        status: "posted",
        relatedBookingId: "bk_1001",
      },
    ]);
  }
  if (!store.invoicesByUser.has(userId)) {
    store.invoicesByUser.set(userId, [
      {
        id: "inv_001",
        createdAtISO: new Date(Date.now() - 86400000).toISOString(),
        status: "paid",
        subtotal: 150,
        tax: 0,
        total: 150,
        currency: "USD",
        bookingId: "bk_1001",
        receiptUrl: "",
        lineItems: [{ id: "li_1", label: "Credits top-up", amount: 150 }],
        paymentMethodSummary: "Visa •••• 4242",
      },
    ]);
  }
  if (!store.liveApptByBooking.has("bk_1001")) {
    store.liveApptByBooking.set("bk_1001", {
      bookingId: "bk_1001",
      state: "scheduled",
      etaISO: new Date(Date.now() + 45 * 60000).toISOString(),
      gps: [],
      photos: [],
      checklist: [
        { id: "c1", label: "Kitchen", completed: false },
        { id: "c2", label: "Bathrooms", completed: false },
        { id: "c3", label: "Floors", completed: false },
      ],
      events: [
        {
          id: "ev_001",
          atISO: new Date().toISOString(),
          type: "note",
          summary: "Appointment created",
          metadata: {},
        },
      ],
    });
  }
}

/**
 * HEALTH
 */
app.get("/health", (_req, res) => res.json({ ok: true, ts: new Date().toISOString() }));

/**
 * TRUST ENDPOINTS (match your frontend hooks)
 */

// GET /api/credits/balance
app.get("/api/credits/balance", requireAuth, (req: AuthedRequest, res) => {
  const userId = req.user!.sub;
  seedUser(userId);

  const b = store.creditsBalanceByUser.get(userId)!;
  res.json(b);
});

// GET /api/credits/ledger?from&to&type&status&search&limit
app.get("/api/credits/ledger", requireAuth, (req: AuthedRequest, res) => {
  const userId = req.user!.sub;
  seedUser(userId);

  const entries = [...(store.ledgerByUser.get(userId) || [])];

  const {
    from,
    to,
    type,
    status,
    search,
    limit = "50",
  } = req.query as Record<string, string | undefined>;

  let filtered = entries;

  if (from) filtered = filtered.filter((e) => e.createdAtISO >= from);
  if (to) filtered = filtered.filter((e) => e.createdAtISO <= to);
  if (type) filtered = filtered.filter((e) => e.type === type);
  if (status) filtered = filtered.filter((e) => e.status === status);
  if (search) {
    const s = search.toLowerCase();
    filtered = filtered.filter((e) =>
      [e.id, e.description, e.relatedBookingId, e.invoiceId].filter(Boolean).some((v: string) => v.toLowerCase().includes(s))
    );
  }

  const lim = Math.max(1, Math.min(200, Number(limit)));
  res.json({ entries: filtered.slice(0, lim) });
});

// GET /api/billing/invoices
app.get("/api/billing/invoices", requireAuth, (req: AuthedRequest, res) => {
  const userId = req.user!.sub;
  seedUser(userId);

  res.json({ invoices: store.invoicesByUser.get(userId) || [] });
});

// GET /api/billing/invoices/:id
app.get("/api/billing/invoices/:id", requireAuth, (req: AuthedRequest, res) => {
  const userId = req.user!.sub;
  seedUser(userId);

  const invoices = store.invoicesByUser.get(userId) || [];
  const invoice = invoices.find((i) => i.id === req.params.id);
  if (!invoice) return res.status(404).json({ message: "Invoice not found" });
  res.json(invoice);
});

// GET /api/appointments/:bookingId/live
app.get("/api/appointments/:bookingId/live", requireAuth, (req: AuthedRequest, res) => {
  const userId = req.user!.sub;
  seedUser(userId);

  const bookingId = req.params.bookingId;
  const live = store.liveApptByBooking.get(bookingId);
  if (!live) return res.status(404).json({ message: "Appointment not found" });

  res.json(live);
});

// POST /api/appointments/:bookingId/events
const AppointmentEventCreateSchema = z.object({
  type: z.enum(["en_route", "arrived", "check_in", "check_out", "note"]),
  note: z.string().optional(),
  gps: z.object({ lat: z.number(), lng: z.number(), accuracyM: z.number().optional() }).optional(),
  source: z.enum(["device", "manual_override"]).optional(),
});

app.post("/api/appointments/:bookingId/events", requireAuth, (req: AuthedRequest, res) => {
  const parsed = AppointmentEventCreateSchema.safeParse(req.body);
  if (!parsed.success) return res.status(400).json({ message: "Invalid payload", details: parsed.error.flatten() });

  const bookingId = req.params.bookingId;
  const live = store.liveApptByBooking.get(bookingId);
  if (!live) return res.status(404).json({ message: "Appointment not found" });

  const nowISO = new Date().toISOString();
  const { type, note, gps, source } = parsed.data;

  // Update state machine (minimal)
  const stateMap: Record<string, string | null> = {
    en_route: "en_route",
    arrived: "arrived",
    check_in: "checked_in",
    check_out: "completed",
    note: null,
  };
  const nextState = stateMap[type];
  if (nextState) live.state = nextState;

  // Append event
  live.events.unshift({
    id: `ev_${Math.random().toString(16).slice(2)}`,
    atISO: nowISO,
    type: type === "note" ? "note" : "state_change",
    summary: type === "note" ? (note || "Note") : `State change: ${type}`,
    metadata: { source: source || "device" },
  });

  // Append GPS evidence if present
  if (gps) {
    live.gps.unshift({
      id: `gps_${Math.random().toString(16).slice(2)}`,
      event: type,
      atISO: nowISO,
      lat: gps.lat,
      lng: gps.lng,
      accuracyM: gps.accuracyM,
      source: source || "device",
    });
    live.events.unshift({
      id: `ev_${Math.random().toString(16).slice(2)}`,
      atISO: nowISO,
      type: "gps",
      summary: `GPS evidence recorded for ${type}`,
      metadata: { ...gps, source: source || "device" },
    });
  }

  res.json({ ok: true });
});

/**
 * START
 */
app.listen(PORT, () => {
  console.log(`✅ Trust backend listening on http://localhost:${PORT}`);
  console.log(`   CORS origin: ${FRONTEND_ORIGIN}`);
});

  }
}

2) Wire the frontend to your backend

3) Confirm auth (this is usually the blocker)
Your note says: “frontend sends token from localStorage via apiClient.”

That means your frontend apiClient must attach:

Authorization: Bearer <token>

If your apiClient does NOT currently do that:
Update your apiClient.ts to include something like:

const token = typeof window !== "undefined" ? localStorage.getItem("token") : null;

headers: {
  ...(token ? { Authorization: `Bearer ${token}` } : {}),
  ...
}
Quick local test token
To test quickly, you can generate a token using the backend secret. For local dev only:

In a node REPL:

const jwt=require("jsonwebtoken");
console.log(jwt.sign({sub:"user_123"}, "dev-secret-change-me"));
Then put that string into frontend localStorage:

localStorage.setItem("token", "<PASTE_TOKEN_HERE>")
Now your Trust pages should load real responses instead of mocks.

4) Remove/disable mock fallback (when ready)
Right now your hooks already try backend first. The remaining “mock fallback” is usually in:

older *.service.ts files

demo pages or mock adapters

Best practice for Trust-Fintech: once backend exists, fail loud (show error state) rather than silently mock.

So:

delete mock branches for production builds

keep mocks only in dev behind a flag like TRUST_USE_MOCKS=true

Key trust rule: events append-only, overrides are new events.

would this question be more for the backend or the ffront end. im going to describe wat is happending, i am logged in with a valid user nam,e and password and i begin to click on different links on the page and many of them do not load and not only that it reloads the log in page and signs me out . do u understand?

Yes — I understand exactly what’s happening.

Short answer:

👉 This is primarily a BACKEND + AUTH + SESSION problem — not a frontend UI problem.

Let me explain clearly.

What you’re experiencing:

You log in successfully ✅

You click links ❌

Pages fail to load

Suddenly you’re redirected to login

You’re “signed out”

That pattern almost always means:

🚨 Your authentication session is being LOST between requests.
Not styling.
Not routing.
Not React.

It’s auth state persistence.

What’s actually happening (technical truth)
Your frontend is calling protected backend endpoints.

The backend responds:

401 Unauthorized
So your frontend says:

"User is not authenticated → redirect to login"

Even though you just logged in.

This happens when ONE of these is broken:

🔴 Root Causes (in order of probability)
1. Your JWT token is NOT being sent on navigation
You said earlier:

frontend sends token from localStorage via apiClient

That means:

If ANY request is missing:

Authorization: Bearer <token>
Backend rejects → frontend logs you out.

Common mistake:

login page saves token

apiClient doesn’t attach it consistently

navigation triggers new requests without token

2. Cookies are being dropped (if cookie auth)
If you’re using cookies:

Possible causes:

cookie domain mismatch

SameSite misconfigured

credentials not included

frontend/backend on different ports without CORS credentials

Result:

Browser silently drops cookie.

Backend sees:

no session
→ logs you out.

3. Your backend restarts or crashes
If backend reloads:

in-memory sessions vanish

JWT secret changes

user appears logged out

4. Your auth middleware is too aggressive
For example:

if (!token) redirect("/login")
Even on pages that shouldn’t require auth.

How to prove which one it is (2 minutes)
Open Chrome DevTools:

Press:
F12
Go to:

Network tab → click any failing request
Look at:

STATUS CODE
Tell me if you see:

401

403

302

307

Then check:

Request Headers:
Do you see:

Authorization: Bearer ....
YES or NO?

Application tab → Storage
Check:

Local Storage:
Do you see your token?

Cookies:
Is anything present?

90% chance fix (very common)
Your apiClient probably does NOT attach token globally.

Fix:

In apiClient.ts, make sure you have:

const token =
  typeof window !== "undefined"
    ? localStorage.getItem("token")
    : null;

headers: {
  ...(token ? { Authorization: `Bearer ${token}` } : {}),
}
If missing → every click logs you out.

Why it FEELS random
Because:

Some routes call backend.
Some don’t.

Routes that DO:
→ backend rejects
→ frontend redirects to login.

Feels “random.”

But it’s deterministic.

Frontend vs Backend responsibility
Backend:
validates token

returns 401

Frontend:
must send token

must not auto-logout on transient failures

So it’s:

🔥 AUTH INTEGRATION BUG (both sides)
Tell me ONLY these 3 things and I’ll pinpoint it:
In Network tab — what status code do you see when it kicks you out?

Is Authorization header present?

Are you using cookies or JWT localStorage?

Answer those, and I’ll give you the exact fix line-for-line.


WHEN I AM TESTING OUR APP AND I AM ON A PAGE AND I CLICK A BUTTON OR LINK THAT DOESNT WORK , SHOULD I BE FIXING THAT PROBLEM ON THE BACKEND OR THE FRONT END?

Great question — and this is exactly the kind of thing that separates “random debugging” from systematic engineering. Let’s make this crystal clear.

Short answer:

👉 It depends on why the button or link doesn’t work.
But you can determine which side in under 60 seconds every time.

I’ll give you a simple decision tree you can follow.

🔥 First principle
A button or link “not working” can only fail in three places:

Frontend didn’t fire the action

Frontend fired it, backend rejected it

Backend accepted it, frontend didn’t handle the response

There is no fourth option.

So we diagnose.

✅ Step 1 — Did the click fire?
Open DevTools:

F12 → Network tab
Click the broken button.

Question:
Do you see ANY network request?

CASE A — NO network request appears
That is a FRONTEND problem.
Examples:

onClick not wired

disabled button

Link href missing

React state blocking navigation

JS error stopping handler

Fix in frontend.
CASE B — YES, a request appears
Click it.

Look at Status Code.

🔴 401 / 403
Backend says:

“You are not authorized.”

This is AUTH INTEGRATION

Usually:

token not sent

cookie missing

session lost

Fix is:

frontend sends auth correctly

backend validates correctly

But primary symptom is backend rejection.

🔴 404
Backend says:

“Route doesn’t exist.”

Backend problem.

Either:

endpoint not implemented

frontend calling wrong path

🔴 500

Yep — this log tells us a LOT. ✅
You have two separate issues:

Next.js metadata warnings (harmless, but fixable)

Socket.IO/WebSocket trying to connect to localhost:4000 and failing with 404 (this one can break features / cause weird “not loading” behavior depending on what uses it)

1) ✅ Next.js warnings: viewport / themeColor in metadata
What it means
In Next.js App Router, viewport + themeColor can’t be inside export const metadata = { ... } anymore for those routes.
They must be exported via export const viewport = { ... } (or generateViewport).

Where it’s happening
/cleaner/ai-assistant/settings

/cleaner/ai-assistant/quick-responses

Fix (copy/paste)
Open each page/layout file that currently has something like:

export const metadata = {
  viewport: "...",
  themeColor: "...",
}
Replace with:

import type { Metadata, Viewport } from "next";

export const metadata: Metadata = {
  title: "Whatever",
  // keep non-viewport metadata here
};

export const viewport: Viewport = {
  themeColor: "#0f172a", // example
  width: "device-width",
  initialScale: 1,
};
✅ These warnings won’t “log you out” — but it’s good hygiene.

2) 🚨 Real problem: Socket.IO WebSocket handshake 404
The key line
WebSocket connection to 'ws://localhost:4000/socket.io/?EIO=4&transport=websocket' failed: Unexpected response code: 404
What it means
Your frontend is trying to connect to a Socket.IO server at:

http://localhost:4000/socket.io

But your backend on port 4000 (the Trust backend / Express backend) does not have Socket.IO installed, so it responds with 404.

So the frontend keeps retrying and spamming errors.

Is this “backend or frontend”?
This is both, but primarily:

✅ Frontend config issue (it’s trying to connect when there isn’t a Socket.IO server)
OR
✅ Backend missing Socket.IO (if you actually intended realtime)

Choose one: Do you WANT realtime Socket.IO right now?
Option A (recommended MVP): Disable Socket.IO for now
If your Trust Live Appointment page is polling with TanStack Query already, you do NOT need Socket.IO yet.

✅ Fix: find where the socket is created and gate it behind a flag.

Search your frontend for:

io(

socket.io-client

createSocket

localhost:4000

socket.io

Then wrap it:

const ENABLE_SOCKET = process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_ENABLE_SOCKET === "true";

export const socket = ENABLE_SOCKET
  ? io(process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_API_BASE_URL!, { transports: ["websocket"] })
  : null;
And in .env.local set:

NEXT_PUBLIC_ENABLE_SOCKET=false
This instantly removes the websocket failures.

Option B: Add Socket.IO server to your backend on port 4000
If you want real-time “live appointment” updates (nice), then implement it.

Install in backend:
cd backend
npm i socket.io
Add this to your backend server startup (Express):
import { createServer } from "http";
import { Server } from "socket.io";

const httpServer = createServer(app);

const io = new Server(httpServer, {
  cors: { origin: FRONTEND_ORIGIN, credentials: true },
});

io.on("connection", (socket) => {
  console.log("✅ socket connected:", socket.id);

  socket.on("join_booking", (bookingId: string) => {
    socket.join(`booking:${bookingId}`);
  });
});

// then replace app.listen with:
httpServer.listen(PORT, () => {
  console.log(`✅ API + Socket.IO on http://localhost:${PORT}`);
});
Then when an appointment event is posted, emit:

io.to(`booking:${bookingId}`).emit("appointment_event", { bookingId, ...payload });
✅ This makes /socket.io exist, so the handshake stops failing.

Why this might be causing “pages don’t load / log out”
Even though WebSocket errors don’t inherently log you out, if your app has logic like:

“if socket fails → clear user context”

“if connection error → reset auth”

“if backend unreachable → treat user as signed out”

…then the repeated errors can trigger auth reset flows.

Your log shows:

“User context cleared”

“User context set”

That suggests your app has a client-side auth context that may be reacting to connection failures.

So we should fix the socket issue first. ✅

What I need from you (one copy/paste) to give you the exact file to edit
In your frontend codebase, do a search for:

socket.io-client or io(

Paste the snippet where it initializes the socket (5–20 lines).
Then I’ll tell you exactly whether to disable it or wire Socket.IO into backend, and exactly how.

Open:

http://localhost:4000/socket.io ❌ currently 404 (expected with your current backend)

So either:

stop frontend from calling socket.io, or

add socket.io server.

Both are valid — MVP-wise I’d disable first.


WILL U GIVE ME THE ESXACT THING I NEED TO PASTE INTO MY FRONT END

Yes ✅ — here are the exact pasteable pieces to stop the Socket.IO spam + stop the Next metadata warnings. This is the fastest “make the app stable” fix for your frontend.

1) Stop the Socket.IO/WebSocket errors (frontend-only fix)
A) Add this to your .env.local (frontend)
# Backend base URL (you already have this)
NEXT_PUBLIC_API_BASE_URL=http://localhost:4000

# Disable Socket.IO until you actually run a Socket.IO server
NEXT_PUBLIC_ENABLE_SOCKET=false
Restart your frontend dev server after editing .env.local.

B) Create this file: src/lib/socket.ts (PASTE EXACTLY)
// src/lib/socket.ts
import { io, type Socket } from "socket.io-client";

let socket: Socket | null = null;

export function getSocket(): Socket | null {
  // Only run in browser
  if (typeof window === "undefined") return null;

  const enabled = process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_ENABLE_SOCKET === "true";
  if (!enabled) return null;

  // Reuse singleton
  if (socket) return socket;

  const baseUrl = process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_API_BASE_URL || "";
  socket = io(baseUrl, {
    transports: ["websocket"],
    withCredentials: true,
  });

  return socket;
}
✅ This guarantees the frontend will NOT attempt ws://localhost:4000/socket.io/... unless you explicitly enable it.

C) Replace your existing Socket.IO initialization with this (PASTE)
Wherever your app currently does something like:

import { io } from "socket.io-client";
const socket = io("http://localhost:4000");
Replace it with:

import { getSocket } from "@/lib/socket";

const socket = getSocket(); // can be null when disabled
And if your code calls socket methods, guard them:

socket?.emit("join_booking", bookingId);
socket?.on("appointment_event", (payload) => {
  console.log(payload);
});
✅ After this, those 404 websocket errors should stop immediately.

2) Fix the Next.js metadata warnings (viewport/themeColor)
The warning says you have viewport and themeColor inside metadata in these routes:

/cleaner/ai-assistant/settings

/cleaner/ai-assistant/quick-responses

Paste this pattern into each affected page/layout file
Find the file for each route (likely page.tsx or layout.tsx) that currently contains:

export const metadata = { ... viewport: ..., themeColor: ... }
Replace with this exact structure:

// at top of the file

  title: "AI Assistant Settings",
  // keep everything EXCEPT viewport/themeColor here
};

export const viewport: Viewport = {
  width: "device-width",
  initialScale: 1,
  themeColor: "#0f172a",
};
Do the same for quick-responses, changing the title if you want.

✅ That removes the “Unsupported metadata viewport/themeColor” warnings.
