WATS THE OTHER OPTION

The “other option” is: keep Socket.IO enabled and add a real Socket.IO server to your backend (so /socket.io stops returning 404). ✅🔁

Right now your frontend is trying to connect to:

ws://localhost:4000/socket.io/...

…but your backend doesn’t implement Socket.IO, so it 404s. The fix is to make your backend speak Socket.IO.

Option B: Add Socket.IO to your backend (exact paste)
1) Install Socket.IO on the backend
In your backend folder:

cd backend
npm i socket.io
(If your backend is TypeScript and you want types, Socket.IO ships types already.)

2) Update your backend server.ts to use an HTTP server
You can’t use app.listen() directly if you want Socket.IO cleanly. You create an HTTP server from Express and attach Socket.IO.

Paste this near the top of backend/src/server.ts
import { createServer } from "http";
import { Server as SocketIOServer } from "socket.io";
Replace your app.listen(...) block with this exact code
const httpServer = createServer(app);

const io = new SocketIOServer(httpServer, {
  cors: {
    origin: FRONTEND_ORIGIN || "http://localhost:3000",
    credentials: true,
  },
});

// Basic connection logging
io.on("connection", (socket) => {
  console.log("✅ Socket connected:", socket.id);

  // Let client subscribe to a booking room for live updates
  socket.on("join_booking", (bookingId: string) => {
    socket.join(`booking:${bookingId}`);
  });

  socket.on("leave_booking", (bookingId: string) => {
    socket.leave(`booking:${bookingId}`);
  });

  socket.on("disconnect", (reason) => {
    console.log("⚠ Socket disconnected:", socket.id, reason);
  });
});

httpServer.listen(PORT, () => {
  console.log(`✅ API + Socket.IO running on http://localhost:${PORT}`);
});
✅ Now your backend will respond to /socket.io correctly and your WebSocket handshake will succeed.

3) Emit events when appointment state changes
In your existing endpoint:
POST /api/appointments/:bookingId/events

After you update the appointment + add events, emit to that booking room:

Add this at the end of that route (before res.json)
io.to(`booking:${bookingId}`).emit("appointment_event", {
  bookingId,
  state: live.state,
  event: parsed.data,
  atISO: new Date().toISOString(),
});
✅ Now the frontend can receive live updates instead of polling.

4) Frontend: Join the booking room (example)
Wherever you load your live appointment page:

import { getSocket } from "@/lib/socket";

const socket = getSocket();
socket?.emit("join_booking", bookingId);

socket?.on("appointment_event", (payload) => {
  console.log("live update:", payload);
  // optionally invalidate TanStack Query here
});
Which option is better right now?
Disable Socket.IO (Option A) if you’re still stabilizing auth + APIs. Polling is fine.

Add Socket.IO (Option B) if you want a truly “live” day-of-service experience and you’re ready to maintain a realtime server.

Given your Trust-Fintech spec: Socket.IO is a nice-to-have, not required (polling still satisfies “evidence-forward” + auditability). But it does make “tracks reality” feel more immediate.

If you tell me what backend you’re running (Express inside Next? separate Express? something else), I’ll tailor the exact patch to your current file structure so you don’t have to adapt anything.


HOW DO I KNOW WAT THINGS I NEEED TO HAVE FOR THE BACK END? LIKE WAT THINGS ON THE FRONT END ARE NOT SUPPORTED IN THE BACKEND?

You decide what the backend must have by applying one rule:

If the frontend needs “truth,” the backend must provide it. ✅

The frontend can display, animate, and collect input — but it cannot be the system of record for anything related to money, identity, permissions, state transitions, or evidence.

Below is a crisp framework you can use every time + a PureTask-specific checklist.

1) The hard boundary: what frontend can’t be trusted to do
Anything a user can change by:

editing the DOM

modifying localStorage

intercepting requests

calling your API directly

…must be enforced/owned by the backend.

So the backend must own:

A) Authentication + sessions
Login verification

Token/session issuance

Token validation and expiration

Role permissions (client/cleaner/admin)

B) Authorization (permissions)
“Is this user allowed to view this booking/ledger/invoice?”

“Is this cleaner assigned to this job?”

“Is this admin allowed to override state?”

C) Money/accounting
Credits ledger entries

Refunds, fees, bonuses

Invoice totals, taxes, receipts

Exportable history

Preventing double charges / double refunds

D) State machines + business rules
Booking status transitions

Appointment transitions (scheduled → en_route → arrived → checked_in → completed)

Preventing illegal transitions (e.g., check_out without check_in)

E) Evidence storage and integrity
GPS check-in/out events with server timestamps

Photo metadata + storage permissions

Checklist completion timestamps

Audit timeline of events (append-only)

Manual override logs with reasons

✅ The frontend must not be able to “declare” these as true without backend validation.

2) What the backend does NOT need to support
These are frontend-only concerns:

UI layout / Tailwind / shadcn components

Drawers/modals behavior (Radix)

Animations (Framer Motion/CSS)

Client-side sorting/filtering (unless you want server-side for scale)

Local-only UI state (which drawer is open, selected compare cards, etc.)

The backend doesn’t “support” these; it just returns data.

3) How to know what endpoints the backend needs (method)
You already have the correct process:

✅ Start from the frontend data contracts + hooks
Every query/mutation in the frontend becomes a backend endpoint.

Do this systematically:
List all frontend hooks:

useCreditsTrust

useBillingTrust

useLiveAppointmentTrust

useReliabilityTrust (or equivalent)

For each hook, list:

URL it calls

request payload

response payload (type)

auth requirement (who can call)

side effects (write to DB, create ledger entry, etc.)

That becomes your backend spec.

4) PureTask “Trust-Fintech backend requirements” (exact checklist) ✅💳
A) Auth + identity
Backend must implement:

POST /api/auth/login → returns token/cookie

GET /api/auth/me → returns user + roles

role-based access: client/cleaner/admin

Frontend-only can’t guarantee login persists. Backend must.

B) Credits (system of record)
Backend must implement:

GET /api/credits/balance

GET /api/credits/ledger?from&to&type&status&search&limit

(later) POST /api/credits/topup

(later) POST /api/credits/refund

(later) export endpoints: GET /api/credits/ledger/export?format=csv

Backend must enforce:

append-only ledger entries

unique IDs

correct totals

user can only see their own ledger

C) Billing / invoices
Backend must implement:

GET /api/billing/invoices

GET /api/billing/invoices/:id

(optional) GET /api/billing/invoices/:id/download?format=pdf

Backend must enforce:

invoice totals are derived from source data

only rightful users can access invoices

D) Live appointment / evidence
Backend must implement:

GET /api/appointments/:bookingId/live

POST /api/appointments/:bookingId/events

POST /api/appointments/:bookingId/photos (presigned upload)

(optional) PATCH /api/appointments/:bookingId/checklist/:itemId

Backend must enforce:

allowed state transitions

server timestamps

evidence integrity

manual overrides logged with reasons and actor role

E) Reliability score (differentiation engine)
Backend must implement:

GET /api/cleaners/:id/reliability

OR embed reliability in cleaner profile responses

Backend must enforce:

computed from actual historical metrics

cannot be manipulated client-side

last-updated timestamp

5) The “unsupported frontend features” question (what it really means)
What you’re asking is basically:

“What UI features require backend support to be real?”

Here are the big ones:

✅ Needs backend support
“I’m logged in” (session)

“This job is completed” (state machine)

“This is GPS verified” (evidence storage + timestamps)

“Here’s your credit ledger” (accounting truth)

“Invoice totals” (billing truth)

“Reliability score” (computed truth)

“Export CSV/PDF” (data generation)

❌ Does NOT need backend support
drawers/modals

animations

styling

how tables look

client-side filtering UI

6) Fast rule: “Can this be faked?”
If a user can fake it by modifying front-end state, it must be backend.

Examples:

user sets state = "completed" in devtools → backend must reject unless valid

user edits “balance = 9999” → backend must compute real balance

user uploads “after photo” but claims it was earlier → backend timestamps

If you want, I can make this brutally concrete for YOUR repo
Paste the contents (or list) of docs/BACKEND_ENDPOINTS.md, and I’ll output:

required DB tables (minimum schema)

exact endpoint implementations

auth rules per route

event-sourcing model for auditability

a “backend DoD checklist” that matches your Trust-Fintech DoD

That’s the cleanest way to ensure the backend supports exactly what the frontend already expects.


# Frontend → Backend Spec

Every frontend Trust hook maps to a backend endpoint. Use this as the backend implementation spec.

---

## 1. useCreditsTrust

### useCreditsBalance

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| **Method** | GET |
| **URL** | /api/credits/balance |
| **Request payload** | None |
| **Response type** | CreditsBalance |
| **Auth** | Bearer token; **client** role |
| **Side effects** | None (read-only) |

**Response shape:**
ts
{
  balance: number;
  currency: 'USD';
  lastUpdatedISO: string; // ISO datetime
}


---

### useCreditsLedger

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| **Method** | GET |
| **URL** | /api/credits/ledger |
| **Query params** | from, to, type, status, search, limit |
| **Request payload** | None |
| **Response type** | { entries: CreditLedgerEntry[] } |
| **Auth** | Bearer token; **client** role |
| **Side effects** | None (read-only) |

**Response shape:**
ts
{
  entries: Array<{
    id: string;
    createdAtISO: string;
    type: 'deposit' | 'spend' | 'refund' | 'bonus' | 'fee';
    amount: number;
    currency: 'USD';
    description: string;
    status: 'pending' | 'posted' | 'reversed';
    relatedBookingId?: string;
    invoiceId?: string;
  }>;
}


---

### useBuyCredits

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| **Method** | POST |
| **URL** | /credits/checkout |
| **Request payload** | BuyCreditsRequest |
| **Response type** | BuyCreditsResponse |
| **Auth** | Bearer token; **client** role |
| **Side effects** | Create checkout session; return redirect URL; frontend redirects user |

**Request shape:**
ts
{
  packageId: string;    // e.g. 'starter', 'standard', 'premium'
  successUrl: string;   // e.g. 'http://localhost:3001/client/credits-trust?success=1'
  cancelUrl: string;    // e.g. 'http://localhost:3001/client/credits-trust?cancel=1'
}


**Response shape (at least one of):**
ts
{
  checkoutUrl?: string;  // URL to redirect for payment (Stripe, etc.)
  url?: string;         // Alternative field name
}

Yep — this spec is exactly what you need to build the backend. ✅ Now the job is: turn each row into a real route + real data + real auth (and remove mock fallbacks on the frontend once the routes are stable).

Below is a practical, implementation-first backend plan that will “just work” with your existing Trust pages/hook contracts.

1) Backend requirements derived from your spec
Your backend must provide four capabilities:

A) Auth gate (Bearer token)
Every endpoint in your spec requires:

Authorization: Bearer <token>

Role checks (client, cleaner, maybe admin)

Participant checks for /appointments/:bookingId/live (client or assigned cleaner)

B) Ledger-grade accounting (credits + invoices)
Credits ledger is append-only

Balance is derived from ledger (or stored but must reconcile)

Invoice payment creates ledger events when paying by credits

C) Appointment event timeline + evidence
/appointments/:bookingId/live must return a combined view:

state + ETA

gps evidence

photo evidence

checklist items

timeline events (append-only)

D) Reliability read endpoint
/cleaners/:cleanerId/reliability returns { reliability }

2) Decide where this backend lives
Two valid deployments:

Option A: Separate API server (recommended for what you’re doing now)
API: http://localhost:4000

Frontend: http://localhost:3000

You must configure CORS.

Option B: Next route handlers (fastest if you want single repo)
Everything under src/app/api/...

No CORS

But more coupling

Your earlier logs show your frontend expects localhost:4000 for API, so I’ll assume Option A.

3) Minimal database model (Postgres) that supports your spec
You can implement with any DB, but Postgres is perfect. Here’s the minimum schema.

Users / roles
users(id, role) where role ∈ client|cleaner|admin

Credits
credit_ledger_entries

id

user_id

type (deposit/spend/refund/bonus/fee)

amount (signed)

currency

status (pending/posted/reversed)

related_booking_id nullable

invoice_id nullable

Balance = SUM(amount) over posted entries (or store a materialized balance but must reconcile).

Billing

You can compute reliability later; store it for now.

4) Endpoint-by-endpoint implementation notes (what to enforce)
✅ GET /api/credits/balance (client)
Backend logic:

auth required

role must be client

compute balance from ledger where status='posted'

return {balance, currency:'USD', lastUpdatedISO}

✅ GET /api/credits/ledger (client)
Backend logic:

auth + client role

filters: from, to, type, status, search, limit

search should match id, description, invoiceId, relatedBookingId

return { entries: [...] } sorted newest-first

✅ POST /credits/checkout (client)
Backend logic:

auth + client role

validate packageId, successUrl, cancelUrl

create Stripe checkout session (or stub for now)

return { checkoutUrl }

Important: This endpoint is not under /api in your spec. Keep it exactly.

✅ GET /api/billing/invoices (client)
Backend logic:

auth + client role

list invoices for user_id

include line items (you can include full line items or minimal—spec expects full lineItems on list item too; safest: include them)

✅ GET /api/billing/invoices/:id (client)
Backend logic:

auth + client role

ensure invoice belongs to that user

return full invoice

✅ POST /client/invoices/:id/pay (client)
Backend logic:

auth + client role

validate payment_method

if credits:

verify sufficient balance

create ledger entry spend linked to invoice

update invoice status paid

if card:

create payment intent/charge

update invoice status paid

return { ok: true }

Trust-fintech requirement: paying by credits must produce a ledger entry that drills down to the invoice.

✅ GET /api/appointments/:bookingId/live (client or cleaner participant)
Backend logic:

auth required

allow if:

user is client for this booking, OR

user is assigned cleaner for this booking

gather:

appointment state + eta

gps events

photos

checklist

events timeline

return LiveAppointment

✅ POST /api/appointments/:bookingId/events (cleaner only)
Backend logic:

auth required

role must be cleaner

cleaner must be assigned to this booking

append event

optionally update state based on type

record gps if present

return { ok: true }

if you choose to return 501 for check_in/check_out, do it exactly as spec says. Otherwise, implement them.

✅ GET /cleaners/:cleanerId/reliability (client)
Backend logic:

auth + client role

return { reliability } with breakdown + explainers

6) The “gotchas” that cause your current logout problem
Based on your earlier behavior (click link → reload login → signed out), the usual root causes are:

A) Frontend not consistently sending Authorization header
Confirm your fetch apiClient attaches the token every time.

B) Backend returns 401 for endpoints the page depends on
If any query fails with 401, your UI likely resets auth context.

C) CORS misconfigured (if separate backend)
For Bearer tokens, you still need to allow:

Access-Control-Allow-Origin: http://localhost:3000

Access-Control-Allow-Headers: Authorization, Content-Type

7) The fastest path to “real backend” without overbuilding
Do it in this order:

Auth middleware (Bearer) + roles (client/cleaner)

Implement read-only endpoints first:

credits balance

credits ledger

invoices list

invoice details

appointments live

cleaner reliability

Implement write endpoints:

appointments events

invoice pay

credits checkout

Once these return real data, remove mock fallbacks.

Testing campaign summary
1. API verification script
Path: scripts/run-api-verification.js
Run: npm run test:api or node scripts/run-api-verification.js
Behavior: Calls all backend endpoints (health, login, credits, billing, live appointment, reliability), records pass/fail and response times
Output: docs/TEST_RESULTS.md with per-endpoint results and suggested fixes for failures
Env: API_BASE, TEST_EMAIL, TEST_PASSWORD
2. E2E tests
tests/e2e/trust/credits-billing-trust.spec.ts — Login as client → credits page (balance, buy credits) → billing page (invoices)
tests/e2e/trust/live-appointment-trust.spec.ts — Login as cleaner → live appointment page
Run:
npx playwright test tests/e2e/trust
3. Campaign doc
Path: docs/TESTING_CAMPAIGN.md
Contents:
Prerequisites and setup
How to run API and E2E tests
Manual smoke checklist (8 flows)
Results log template
Troubleshooting for: timeouts, 401, 403, 404, CORS, invalid response shape, E2E login issues
CI integration notes.#!/usr/bin/env node
/**
 * API Verification Script
 * Tests all frontend-specified backend endpoints and writes results to docs/TEST_RESULTS.md
 *
 * Usage:
 *   node scripts/run-api-verification.js
 *   API_BASE=http://localhost:4000 node scripts/run-api-verification.js
 *   TEST_EMAIL=client@test.com TEST_PASSWORD=TestPass123! node scripts/run-api-verification.js
 */

const fs = require('fs');
const path = require('path');

const API_BASE = process.env.API_BASE || 'http://localhost:4000';
const TEST_EMAIL = process.env.TEST_EMAIL || 'client@test.com';
const TEST_PASSWORD = process.env.TEST_PASSWORD || 'TestPass123!';

const results = [];
let token = null;

function log(name, ok, status, durationMs, message = '', solution = '') {
  results.push({ name, ok, status, durationMs, message, solution });
  const icon = ok ? '✓' : '✗';
  console.log(${icon} ${name} (${status} ${durationMs}ms)${message ? ': ' + message : ''});
}

async function fetchJson(url, opts = {}) {
  const start = Date.now();
  const res = await fetch(url, {
    ...opts,
    headers: {
      'Content-Type': 'application/json',
      Accept: 'application/json',
      ...(token ? { Authorization: Bearer ${token} } : {}),
      ...(opts.headers || {}),
    },
  });
  const durationMs = Date.now() - start;
  let body;
  try {
    body = await res.json();
  } catch {
    body = await res.text();
  }
  return { res, body, durationMs };
}

async function run() {
  console.log('\n=== API Verification Campaign ===');
  console.log(Base URL: ${API_BASE});
  console.log('');

  // 1. Health (no auth)
  try {
    const { res, durationMs } = await fetchJson(${API_BASE}/health);
    const ok = res.ok;
    log('GET /health', ok, res.status, durationMs, ok ? '' : res.statusText);
    if (!ok) {
      results[results.length - 1].solution =
        'Backend not running. Start backend on port 4000. Check NEXT_PUBLIC_API_URL in .env.local.';
    }
  } catch (e) {
    log('GET /health', false, 0, 0, e.message);
    results[results.length - 1].solution =
      'Connection refused or timeout. Ensure backend is running at ' +
      API_BASE +
      ' and CORS allows requests.';
  }

  // 2. Login to get token
  try {
    const { res, body, durationMs } = await fetchJson(${API_BASE}/auth/login, {
      method: 'POST',
      body: JSON.stringify({ email: TEST_EMAIL, password: TEST_PASSWORD }),
    });
    const ok = res.ok && body?.token;
    if (ok) token = body.token;
    log(
      'POST /auth/login',
      ok,
      res.status,
      durationMs,
      ok ? '' : (body?.message || body?.error?.message || 'No token in response'),
      ok ? '' : 'Create test user via POST /auth/register. Ensure response includes { token, user }.'
    );
  } catch (e) {
    log('POST /auth/login', false, 0, 0, e.message);
    results[results.length - 1].solution =
      'Network error. Check backend is running. Ensure TEST_EMAIL and TEST_PASSWORD are valid.';
  }

  if (!token) {
    console.log('\nNo token — skipping authenticated endpoints.\n');
    writeReport();
    return;
  }

  // 3. Credits
  try {
    const { res, body, durationMs } = await fetchJson(${API_BASE}/api/credits/balance);
    const ok = res.ok && typeof body?.balance === 'number';
    log(
      'GET /api/credits/balance',
      ok,
      res.status,
      durationMs,
      ok ? balance=${body.balance} : (body?.message || 'Invalid shape'),
      !ok && res.status === 401
        ? 'Token invalid. Re-login. Check Authorization header is sent.'
        : !ok && res.status === 403
          ? 'Client role required.'
          : ''
    );
  } catch (e) {
    log('GET /api/credits/balance', false, 0, 0, e.message);
    results[results.length - 1].solution = 'CORS or network error. Check backend allows Origin.';
  }

  try {
    const { res, body, durationMs } = await fetchJson(${API_BASE}/api/credits/ledger?limit=5);
    const ok = res.ok && Array.isArray(body?.entries);
    log(
      'GET /api/credits/ledger',
      ok,
      res.status,
      durationMs,
      ok ? entries=${body.entries.length} : (body?.message || 'Invalid shape'),
      !ok ? 'Response must be { entries: CreditLedgerEntry[] }' : ''
    );
  } catch (e) {
    log('GET /api/credits/ledger', false, 0, 0, e.message);
  }

  try {
    const { res, body, durationMs } = await fetchJson(${API_BASE}/credits/checkout, {
      method: 'POST',
      body: JSON.stringify({
        packageId: 'starter',
        successUrl: 'http://localhost:3001/client/credits-trust?success=1',
        cancelUrl: 'http://localhost:3001/client/credits-trust?cancel=1',
      }),
    });
    const ok = res.ok && (body?.checkoutUrl || body?.url);
    log(
      'POST /credits/checkout',
      ok,
      res.status,
      durationMs,
      ok ? 'checkoutUrl returned' : (body?.message || 'Missing checkoutUrl/url'),
      !ok
        ? 'Response must include checkoutUrl or url for redirect to payment provider.'
        : ''
    );
  } catch (e) {
    log('POST /credits/checkout', false, 0, 0, e.message);
  }

  // 4. Billing
  try {
    const { res, body, durationMs } = await fetchJson(${API_BASE}/api/billing/invoices);
    const ok = res.ok && Array.isArray(body?.invoices);
    log(
      'GET /api/billing/invoices',
      ok,
      res.status,
      durationMs,
      ok ? invoices=${body.invoices.length} : (body?.message || 'Invalid shape'),
      !ok ? 'Response must be { invoices: Invoice[] }' : ''
    );
  } catch (e) {
    log('GET /api/billing/invoices', false, 0, 0, e.message);
  }

  try {
    const { res, durationMs } = await fetchJson(
      ${API_BASE}/api/billing/invoices/test-invalid-id
    );
    const ok = res.status === 404 || res.ok;
    log(
      'GET /api/billing/invoices/:id (404)',
      ok,
      res.status,
      durationMs,
      ok ? '404 or 200 expected' : 'Unexpected error',
      ''
    );
  } catch (e) {
    log('GET /api/billing/invoices/:id', false, 0, 0, e.message);
  }

  try {
    const { res, durationMs } = await fetchJson(
      ${API_BASE}/client/invoices/test-invalid-id/pay,
      {
        method: 'POST',
        body: JSON.stringify({ payment_method: 'credits' }),
      }
    );
    const ok = res.status === 404 || res.status === 400 || res.status === 422;
    log(
      'POST /client/invoices/:id/pay (expect 404/400 for invalid)',
      ok,
      res.status,
      durationMs,
      ok ? 'Expected error for invalid id' : 'Unexpected response',
      ''
    );
  } catch (e) {
    log('POST /client/invoices/:id/pay', false, 0, 0, e.message);
  }

  // 5. Live appointment
  try {
    const { res, body, durationMs } = await fetchJson(
      ${API_BASE}/api/appointments/test-booking-id/live
    );
    const ok = res.ok || res.status === 404;
    log(
      'GET /api/appointments/:bookingId/live',
      ok,
      res.status,
      durationMs,
      ok ? (res.ok ? 'OK' : '404 for unknown booking') : 'Unexpected error',
      !ok && res.status === 401 ? 'Token required. Client or cleaner role.' : ''
    );
  } catch (e) {
    log('GET /api/appointments/:bookingId/live', false, 0, 0, e.message);
  }

  try {
    const { res, durationMs } = await fetchJson(
      ${API_BASE}/api/appointments/test-booking-id/events,
      {
        method: 'POST',
        body: JSON.stringify({
          type: 'en_route',
          gps: { lat: 37.77, lng: -122.42, accuracyM: 10 },
          source: 'device',
        }),
      }
    );
    const ok = res.ok || res.status === 404 || res.status === 403 || res.status === 501;
    log(
      'POST /api/appointments/:bookingId/events',
      ok,
      res.status,
      durationMs,
      ok ? 'OK or expected error' : 'Unexpected error',
      res.status === 501
        ? 'check_in/check_out may return 501 — use main tracking API.'
        : ''
    );
  } catch (e) {
    log('POST /api/appointments/:bookingId/events', false, 0, 0, e.message);
  }

  // 6. Reliability
  try {
    const { res, body, durationMs } = await fetchJson(
      ${API_BASE}/cleaners/test-cleaner-id/reliability
    );
    const ok = res.ok || res.status === 404;
    log(
      'GET /cleaners/:cleanerId/reliability',
      ok,
      res.status,
      durationMs,
      ok ? (res.ok ? 'OK' : '404 for unknown cleaner') : 'Unexpected error',
      ''
    );
  } catch (e) {
    log('GET /cleaners/:cleanerId/reliability', false, 0, 0, e.message);
  }

  writeReport();
}

function writeReport() {
  const passed = results.filter((r) => r.ok).length;
  const total = results.length;
  const ts = new Date().toISOString();

  let md = # API Verification Results\n\n;
  md += **Run:** ${ts}\n;
  md += **Base URL:** ${API_BASE}\n;
  md += **Summary:** ${passed}/${total} passed\n\n;
  md += ---\n\n;
  md += | # | Endpoint | Status | Duration | Result |\n;
  md += |---|----------|--------|----------|--------|\n;

  results.forEach((r, i) => {
    const icon = r.ok ? '✓' : '✗';
    const status = r.status || '—';
    const dur = r.durationMs ?? '—';
    const msg = (r.message || '').slice(0, 50);
    md += | ${i + 1} | ${r.name} | ${status} | ${dur}ms | ${icon} ${msg} |\n;
  });

  md += \n---\n\n## Solutions for Failures\n\n;
  const failures = results.filter((r) => !r.ok);
  if (failures.length === 0) {
    md += All tests passed. No solutions needed.\n;
  } else {
    failures.forEach((r) => {
      md += ### ${r.name}\n;
      md += - **Message:** ${r.message || 'N/A'}\n;
      md += - **Solution:** ${r.solution || 'See TRUST_BACKEND_INTEGRATION.md and FRONTEND_TO_BACKEND_SPEC.md'}\n\n;
    });
  }

  const outPath = path.join(__dirname, '..', 'docs', 'TEST_RESULTS.md');
  fs.writeFileSync(outPath, md, 'utf8');
  console.log(\nReport written to ${outPath}\n);
}

run().catch((e) => {
  console.error(e);
  process.exit(1);
});

|---|----------|--------|----------|--------|
| 1 | GET /health | — | 0ms | ✗ fetch failed |
| 2 | POST /auth/login | — | 0ms | ✗ fetch failed |

---

## Solutions for Failures

### GET /health
- **Message:** fetch failed
- **Solution:** Connection refused or timeout. Ensure backend is running at http://localhost:4000 and CORS allows requests.

### POST /auth/login
- **Message:** fetch failed
- **Solution:** Network error. Check backend is running. Ensure TEST_EMAIL and TEST_PASSWORD are valid.

// tests/e2e/trust/credits-billing-trust.spec.ts
// E2E tests for Trust credits and billing flows

import { test, expect } from '@playwright/test';

const CLIENT_EMAIL = process.env.TEST_EMAIL || 'client@test.com';
const CLIENT_PASSWORD = process.env.TEST_PASSWORD || 'TestPass123!';

test.describe('Trust Credits & Billing E2E', () => {
  test.beforeEach(async ({ page }) => {
    await page.goto('/auth/login');
    await page.getByLabel(/email/i).fill(CLIENT_EMAIL);
    await page.getByLabel(/password/i).fill(CLIENT_PASSWORD);
    await page.getByRole('button', { name: /login/i }).click();
    await expect(page).toHaveURL(/\/(client|client\/dashboard)/);
  });

  test('credits-trust page loads and shows balance section', async ({ page }) => {
    await page.goto('/client/credits-trust');
    await expect(page.getByRole('heading', { name: /credits/i })).toBeVisible();
    await expect(page.getByText(/balance/i)).toBeVisible();
    await expect(page.getByRole('button', { name: /buy credits/i })).toBeVisible();
  });

  test('credits-trust page has ledger filters', async ({ page }) => {
    await page.goto('/client/credits-trust');
    await expect(page.getByPlaceholder(/search/i)).toBeVisible();
    await expect(page.getByRole('combobox')).toBeVisible();
  });

  test('billing-trust page loads and shows invoices section', async ({ page }) => {
    await page.goto('/client/billing-trust');
    await expect(page.getByRole('heading', { name: /billing/i })).toBeVisible();
    await expect(page.getByText(/invoices/i)).toBeVisible();
  });

  test('billing-trust page has invoices table or empty state', async ({ page }) => {
    await page.goto('/client/billing-trust');
    await expect(page.getByRole('heading', { name: /billing/i })).toBeVisible();
    await page.waitForTimeout(2000);
    const table = page.locator('table');
    const noData = page.getByText(/failed|loading|no invoices/i);
    await expect(table.or(noData)).toBeVisible();
  });
});
// tests/e2e/trust/live-appointment-trust.spec.ts
// E2E tests for Trust live appointment flow

import { test, expect } from '@playwright/test';

const CLEANER_EMAIL = process.env.TEST_CLEANER_EMAIL || 'cleaner@test.com';
const CLEANER_PASSWORD = process.env.TEST_CLEANER_PASSWORD || 'TestPass123!';

test.describe('Trust Live Appointment E2E', () => {
  test.beforeEach(async ({ page }) => {
    await page.goto('/auth/login');
    await page.getByLabel(/email/i).fill(CLEANER_EMAIL);
    await page.getByLabel(/password/i).fill(CLEANER_PASSWORD);
    await page.getByRole('button', { name: /login/i }).click();
    await expect(page).toHaveURL(/\/(cleaner|cleaner\/dashboard)/);
  });

  test('live-trust page loads for valid booking id', async ({ page }) => {
    await page.goto('/client/appointments/test-booking-id/live-trust');
    await expect(page.getByRole('heading', { name: /live|appointment/i })).toBeVisible();
  });

  test('live-trust page shows state or loading', async ({ page }) => {
    await page.goto('/client/appointments/test-booking-id/live-trust');
    await page.waitForTimeout(3000);
    const hasContent =
      page.getByText(/scheduled|en_route|arrived|completed|loading|failed/i);
    await expect(hasContent).toBeVisible();
  });
});
# Testing Campaign: End-to-End + API Verification

Systematic testing of frontend–backend integration with documented results and solutions.

---

## 1. Overview

| Phase | What | Output |
|-------|------|--------|
| **API Verification** | Script hits all backend endpoints | docs/TEST_RESULTS.md |
| **E2E Trust Flows** | Playwright tests (login → credits → billing → live) | HTML report |
| **Manual Smoke** | Quick human verification | Notes in Results Log |

---

## 2. Prerequisites

- Backend running on http://localhost:4000
- Frontend running on http://localhost:3001
- Test users:
  - **Client:** client@test.com / TestPass123! (or set TEST_EMAIL, TEST_PASSWORD)
  - **Cleaner:** cleaner@test.com / TestPass123! (or set TEST_CLEANER_EMAIL, TEST_CLEANER_PASSWORD)

---

## 3. Run API Verification

Tests all endpoints from [FRONTEND_TO_BACKEND_SPEC.md](./FRONTEND_TO_BACKEND_SPEC.md).

bash
node scripts/run-api-verification.js


With custom config:

bash
API_BASE=http://localhost:4000 TEST_EMAIL=client@test.com TEST_PASSWORD=YourPass node scripts/run-api-verification.js


**Output:** docs/TEST_RESULTS.md — pass/fail per endpoint + suggested solutions for failures.

---

## 4. Run E2E Tests

Requires Playwright (npm install -D @playwright/test if needed).

bash
npx playwright test tests/e2e/trust


Full campaign (all E2E):

bash
npx playwright test


Generate HTML report:

bash
npx playwright test tests/e2e/trust --reporter=html
npx playwright show-report


---

## 5. Manual Smoke Checklist

| # | Flow | Steps | Expected | Pass? |
|---|------|-------|----------|-------|
| 1 | Health | Open http://localhost:4000/health | {"ok":true} | |
| 2 | Login | Login as client at /auth/login | Redirect to dashboard | |
| 3 | Credits | Go to /client/credits-trust | Balance + ledger visible | |
| 4 | Buy credits | Click Buy credits, pick package | Redirect to checkout or error | |
| 5 | Billing | Go to /client/billing-trust | Invoices list or empty | |
| 6 | Pay invoice | If unpaid invoice, click Pay | Success toast or error | |
| 7 | Live appointment | Go to /client/appointments/{id}/live-trust | State/checklist visible | |
| 8 | API test page | Go to /api-test | Health Check + Protected Route pass | |

---

## 6. Results Log Template

Copy and fill after each run:

markdown
## Test Run: YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM

- **API Verification:** X/Y passed (see docs/TEST_RESULTS.md)
- **E2E Trust:** X/Y passed
- **Manual Smoke:** X/8 passed

### Failures

| Test | Error | Solution applied |
|------|-------|------------------|
| ... | ... | ... |


---

## 7. Solutions for Common Failures

### Connection timeout

| Cause | Solution |
|-------|----------|
| Backend not running | Start backend: cd puretask-backend && npm run dev |
| Wrong port | Set NEXT_PUBLIC_API_URL=http://localhost:4000 in .env.local |
| Firewall/VPN | Disable or allow localhost |

### 401 Unauthorized

| Cause | Solution |
|-------|----------|
| No token | Ensure user is logged in; token in localStorage under puretask_token |
| Token expired | Re-login |
| Wrong auth header | Backend expects Authorization: Bearer <token> |
| Auth endpoint returns wrong shape | Backend must return { token, user } from /auth/login |

### 403 Forbidden

| Cause | Solution |
|-------|----------|
| Wrong role | Credits/billing require **client**; post event requires **cleaner** |
| Not job participant | Live appointment requires client or cleaner assigned to that job |

### 404 Not Found

| Cause | Solution |
|-------|----------|
| Endpoint not implemented | Implement per [FRONTEND_TO_BACKEND_SPEC.md](./FRONTEND_TO_BACKEND_SPEC.md) |
| Wrong path | Use exact paths: /api/credits/balance, /api/billing/invoices, etc. |

### CORS errors

| Cause | Solution |
|-------|----------|
| Origin not allowed | Backend CORS must allow http://localhost:3001 |
| Credentials | Backend credentials: true; frontend credentials: 'include' |

### Invalid response shape

| Endpoint | Required shape | Fix |
|----------|----------------|-----|
| /api/credits/balance | { balance, currency, lastUpdatedISO } | Backend returns exact fields |
| /api/credits/ledger | { entries: [...] } | Backend returns entries array |
| /api/billing/invoices | { invoices: [...] } | Backend returns invoices array |
| /credits/checkout | { checkoutUrl } or { url } | Backend returns redirect URL |

### E2E: Login fails

| Cause | Solution |
|-------|----------|
| Test user doesn't exist | Create via POST /auth/register or seed script |
| Wrong credentials | Set TEST_EMAIL, TEST_PASSWORD env vars |
| Redirect path differs | Update test toHaveURL pattern |

### E2E: Page not found

| Cause | Solution |
|-------|----------|
| Route doesn't exist | Ensure /client/credits-trust, /client/billing-trust exist |
| Protected route redirect | Login before navigating; check ProtectedRoute |

---

## 8. Files Reference

| File | Purpose |
|------|---------|
| scripts/run-api-verification.js | API verification script |
| docs/TEST_RESULTS.md | Auto-generated API results |
| tests/e2e/trust/credits-billing-trust.spec.ts | E2E credits + billing |
| tests/e2e/trust/live-appointment-trust.spec.ts | E2E live appointment |
| [FRONTEND_TO_BACKEND_SPEC.md](./FRONTEND_TO_BACKEND_SPEC.md) | Endpoint contracts |
| [TRUST_BACKEND_INTEGRATION.md](./TRUST_BACKEND_INTEGRATION.md) | Auth, errors, CORS |

---

## 9. CI Integration

Add to your CI pipeline:

yaml
# Example GitHub Actions
- name: Start backend
  run: cd puretask-backend && npm run dev &
- name: Start frontend
  run: npm run dev &
- name: Wait for servers
  run: sleep 10
- name: API verification
  run: node scripts/run-api-verification.js
- name: E2E tests
  run: npx playwright test tests/e2e/trust


Yep — I understand what you pasted. ✅ And the key signal is this:

API Verification Results: 0/2 passed
GET /health → fetch failed
POST /auth/login → fetch failed

That means your script cannot reach the backend at all. This is not a “wrong response shape” issue yet — it’s connectivity (backend not running / wrong port / wrong URL).

Here’s exactly how to fix it, in the most deterministic order.

1) Fix the root cause: “fetch failed” = backend unreachable
A) Confirm the backend is running on the right port
Open a terminal and run:

curl http://localhost:4000/health
Expected:

{"ok":true}
If that fails, the backend is not running on 4000 (or not running at all).

B) Start backend on 4000
From your backend directory:

cd backend
npm run dev
Then re-test:

curl http://localhost:4000/health
2) Your docs show a port mismatch (important)
Your campaign doc says:

Backend: http://localhost:4000

Frontend: http://localhost:3001

…but most Next apps default to 3000 unless you changed it.

✅ This matters for CORS and redirect URLs.

If your frontend is actually on 3000:
Update your test script/campaign docs OR set frontend to 3001.

To run Next on 3001:

PORT=3001 npm run dev
3) Your API script assumes /auth/login exists
Your script calls:

POST http://localhost:4000/auth/login

So your backend must implement:

POST /auth/login returning { token } (at minimum)

Ideally { token, user }

If you’re using the earlier Trust backend I drafted that only had Bearer middleware but no login route, the script will fail on login even when health works.

✅ Minimal login route requirement:

Backend must implement:
POST /auth/login ✅

(Optional but recommended) POST /auth/register for seeding test users

4) Fix CORS (only if frontend and backend differ)
If frontend is on 3001 and backend on 4000, backend CORS must allow:

http://localhost:3001 (or 3000 if that’s your actual frontend)

In Express, it should look like:

app.use(cors({ origin: "http://localhost:3001", credentials: true }));
But note: your API verification script runs from Node, not the browser — so CORS does not block the script.
CORS only blocks browser requests.

So for the script’s “fetch failed,” CORS is NOT the first suspect. It’s almost always backend not running / wrong URL / wrong port.

5) Run your verification script correctly
From repo root:

node scripts/run-api-verification.js
Or with explicit env:

API_BASE=http://localhost:4000 TEST_EMAIL=client@test.com TEST_PASSWORD=TestPass123! node scripts/run-api-verification.js
If GET /health passes but login fails, your backend is reachable but missing /auth/login or returning wrong shape.

The fastest “make it green” plan ✅
Do this in order:

Start backend on 4000

Make sure GET /health returns ok

Implement POST /auth/login returning { token }

Ensure test user exists (client@test.com)

Re-run node scripts/run-api-verification.js

Only after those 5 steps should you start worrying about credits/billing endpoints.

http://localhost:4000/health

(A) JSON { ok: true }

(B) “This site can’t be reached”

(C) something else (404/HTML/etc.)

Reply with A/B/C and I’ll tell you the exact next fix (including whether you’re running the wrong backend folder or wrong port).

Now you need the backend up on http://localhost:4000 (your test script + Trust hooks are pointed there). Your earlier TEST_RESULTS.md shows fetch failed, which means the backend is not reachable yet.

Here’s the exact checklist to get them working together (zero guesswork):

1) Confirm backend is running (fastest check)

Backend should allow:

From repo root:

✅ GET /health passes

POST /auth/login returning { token }

5) Critical note: Your backend MUST implement /auth/login
Your script calls:

POST http://localhost:4000/auth/login

So your backend must have that route.

If your backend currently only has /api/credits/... but no /auth/login, the script will fail.

This console dump is basically saying: (1) you have a harmless Next.js metadata warning, and (2) your frontend is calling backend endpoints that either don’t exist (404) or are crashing (500). ✅

I’ll decode each part and tell you exactly what to fix.

1) “Unsupported metadata viewport/themeColor…” (NOT breaking anything)
Meaning
In Next.js App Router, you can’t put viewport or themeColor inside:

export const metadata = { ... }
Next wants them exported separately as export const viewport = ....

Fix (copy/paste)
In the file for /cleaner/dashboard (likely src/app/cleaner/dashboard/page.tsx or layout.tsx), do this:

import type { Metadata, Viewport } from "next";

export const metadata: Metadata = {
  title: "Cleaner Dashboard",
  // keep only non-viewport metadata here
};

export const viewport: Viewport = {
  width: "device-width",
  initialScale: 1,
  themeColor: "#0f172a",
};
✅ This removes the warnings.
❗It does not fix your loading/logouts.

2) GET http://localhost:4000/bookings/me 404 (Not Found)
Meaning
Your frontend is calling /bookings/me, but your backend at localhost:4000 does not have that route.

So your Cleaner Dashboard cannot load bookings → UI breaks or shows errors.

Fix options
Backend fix (correct): implement:

GET /bookings/me

OR

Frontend fix (temporary): point the dashboard to a route that exists, or show an empty state when 404.

Given your Trust backend spec, /bookings/me is not part of Trust hooks — it’s part of your “main PureTask API”.

So either:

you’re running the Trust backend only (minimal endpoints)

but the frontend dashboard expects the full PureTask backend.

✅ That’s why you’re seeing 404s.

3) GET /cleaner/dashboard/analytics?period=month 500
Meaning
This endpoint exists, but your backend throws an internal error.

500 = backend bug (crash, missing DB tables, null reference, etc.)

Fix
You must inspect backend logs for the stack trace.
In the backend terminal, it’ll show exactly why it crashed.

Typical causes:

DB connection missing

query fails (table missing)

code assumes a user exists but auth/user lookup fails

4) GET /cleaners/<id>/reviews ... 404
Meaning
Backend does not implement cleaner reviews endpoint:

GET /cleaners/:cleanerId/reviews

So your “FiveStarReviewWatcher” component fails.

✅ Again: frontend expects full API, but backend doesn’t have it.

5) Lottie preload warning (minor)
“resource … was preloaded but not used…”

Harmless performance warning. Not related to auth/logouts.

The real takeaway 🚨
You are currently running a backend on localhost:4000 that is missing major endpoints your dashboard depends on.

So pages “don’t work” because:

some endpoints return 404 (not implemented)

some return 500 (backend crashing)

This is exactly what a partially-implemented backend looks like.

What you should do next (best path)
Step A — Decide: are you trying to run…
1) ONLY Trust-Fintech pages?
If yes: use these pages to test:

/client/credits-trust

/client/billing-trust

/client/appointments/:id/live-trust

…and ignore /cleaner/dashboard for now because it depends on non-trust endpoints.

2) The FULL app (dashboards, bookings, reviews, analytics)?
If yes: your backend must implement at least:

GET /bookings/me

GET /cleaner/dashboard/analytics

GET /cleaner/goals

GET /cleaners/:id/reviews

plus whatever /auth/login uses

Quick way to identify what backend you actually need ✅
Open your backend terminal and confirm which server you’re running:

If it logs only /api/credits/*, /api/billing/*, /api/appointments/* → Trust backend only

If it’s meant to be PureTask main backend, it must contain those dashboard routes.

Right now your frontend is clearly built expecting the main backend, not just Trust.

If you want a concrete “paste” fix right now
I can give you paste-ready Express route stubs for these endpoints so the dashboard stops exploding (returns empty safe shapes instead of 404/500), like:

/bookings/me → { bookings: [] }

/cleaner/dashboard/analytics → { ...defaults }

/cleaner/goals → { goals: [] }

/cleaners/:id/reviews → { reviews: [], page, per_page, total: 0 }

That will immediately stabilize the UI while you build real DB-backed services.

Tell me ONE thing and I’ll generate the exact backend stubs
When you run your backend on 4000, is it:

the Trust backend you created (credits/billing/live only), or

your real PureTask backend repo?

If you paste the backend’s server.ts (or the file where routes are registered), I’ll output the exact additions for those missing endpoints.

Promise.all @ VM860 <anonymous>:1
initializeElement @ react-server-dom-turbopack-client.browser.development.js:1932
VM860 <anonymous>:1  Server  ⚠ Unsupported metadata themeColor is configured in metadata export in /notifications. Please move it to viewport export instead.
Read more: https://ne

You’re seeing the same two Next.js warnings again, just for the /notifications route this time. ✅ Nothing “crashing” here—this is a framework warning about where you declared viewport + themeColor.

What it means 🧠
In Next.js App Router, these fields are NOT supported inside:

export const metadata = { ... }
Specifically:

viewport

themeColor

Next is telling you: “Move those to the viewport export instead.”

So somewhere under app/notifications/* you have something like:

export const metadata = {
  viewport: "width=device-width, initial-scale=1",
  themeColor: "#000",
}
…and Next is warning you.

The fix ✅ (copy/paste)
In your Notifications route file (usually one of these):

src/app/notifications/layout.tsx ✅ best place

OR src/app/notifications/page.tsx

Do:

import type { Metadata, Viewport } from "next";

export const metadata: Metadata = {
  title: "Notifications",
  // keep other metadata here (description, openGraph, etc.)
};

export const viewport: Viewport = {
  width: "device-width",
  initialScale: 1,
  themeColor: "#0f172a", // put themeColor HERE
};
Then remove viewport + themeColor from your metadata object.

Why you see a massive stack trace 📚
That huge dump is just Next’s dev tooling showing where the warning was emitted while navigating.

Key clue:

navigate / linkClicked → you clicked a link to /notifications

<Next.MetadataOutlet> → Next is processing metadata

warning fires

So the stack trace is noise—the actual issue is just the metadata placement.

If you want to fix it across the whole app fast ⚡
Search your codebase for:

viewport: inside metadata

themeColor: inside metadata

Example ripgrep:

rg "export const metadata|viewport:|themeColor:" src/app -n
Any file where you find viewport: or themeColor: inside metadata → move those to export const viewport.

Priority check ✅
These warnings are non-blocking.
Your real “app broken” issues are still the 404/500 API calls you posted earlier.

If you paste your app/notifications/layout.tsx (or whichever file has export const metadata), I’ll point to the exact lines to change.


wat does this mean

Okay — let’s slow this down and translate it into plain English. You’re staring at a wall of DevTools noise, so here’s the simple truth:

You are seeing three completely different things mixed together:

✅ 1. Next.js metadata warning (harmless)
This part:

⚠ Unsupported metadata viewport / themeColor

Means:

👉 You put viewport and themeColor inside:

export const metadata = { ... }
Next.js wants them here instead:

export const viewport = { ... }
Result:
Nothing breaks.
Just a warning.

Fix later. Not urgent.

❌ 2. 404 errors (backend routes DO NOT EXIST)
Example:

GET http://localhost:4000/bookings/me 404
Means:

👉 Your frontend asked your backend:

“Give me my bookings”

Backend replied:

“I don’t have that endpoint.”

Same for:

/cleaners/:id/reviews

/bookings/me

Translation:
Your backend does NOT implement these routes.

Frontend expects them.

So UI breaks.

This is 100% BACKEND missing endpoints.

💥 3. 500 errors (backend is crashing)
Example:

GET /cleaner/dashboard/analytics 500
GET /cleaner/goals 500
Means:

👉 Backend route exists
👉 Backend code throws an exception

Typical causes:

database not connected

table missing

undefined user

bad SQL

This is 100% BACKEND bugs.

🧠 Why you feel “everything is broken”
Because:

Frontend loads

Immediately calls ~6 backend endpoints

3 return 404

2 return 500

React Query retries

Auth context resets

UI collapses

It feels random.

It’s not.

It’s deterministic backend failure.

🔑 The real situation (important)
Right now:

You are running a partial backend (Trust-Fintech)

But your frontend is the FULL PureTask app

So the frontend expects:

bookings

dashboards

analytics

reviews

goals

But backend only has:

credits

billing

appointments

That mismatch causes chaos.

✅ Your choices (pick ONE)
OPTION A — Only test Trust pages (fast)
Ignore dashboards.

Use:

/client/credits-trust
/client/billing-trust
/client/appointments/:id/live-trust
Those match your backend.

OPTION B — Stub missing backend endpoints (recommended)
Add fake routes so UI stops crashing.

Example Express stubs:

app.get("/bookings/me", (req,res)=>res.json({ bookings: [] }));

app.get("/cleaner/dashboard/analytics", (req,res)=>
  res.json({ jobs:0, earnings:0, rating:5 })
);

app.get("/cleaner/goals", (req,res)=>res.json({ goals: [] }));

app.get("/cleaners/:id/reviews", (req,res)=>
  res.json({ reviews: [], page:1, per_page:20, total:0 })
);
This stabilizes frontend immediately.

🧭 Mental model going forward
Yellow warnings
→ framework

404
→ backend missing endpoint

500
→ backend crashing

UI reloads login
→ auth lost because backend failed

Final answer to “what does this mean?”
It means:

👉 Your frontend is healthy
👉 Your backend is incomplete

That’s it.

api.ts:52 API Error: {url: '/cleaner/holiday-overrides', method: 'get', status: 500, data: {…}}

You’ve got two different failures happening on the Calendar page. They’re related, but not the same. 🧭

1) GET /cleaner/holiday-settings → 500
Meaning: the route exists (or is being routed), but your backend handler is throwing.

Common causes (ranked):

Auth context missing → handler expects req.user.cleanerId (or similar) but req.user is undefined → boom 500

DB query failing → table missing / column mismatch / connection failure

Serializer mismatch → code assumes a row exists, tries to read fields from null

What to do (fastest)
In your backend logs for that request, look for the real stack trace. You want the first error line, usually something like:

Cannot read properties of undefined (reading 'id')

relation "cleaner_holiday_settings" does not exist

invalid input syntax for type uuid

If you don’t have backend logging, add this middleware temporarily:

app.use((err, req, res, next) => {
  console.error("API ERROR:", req.method, req.originalUrl, err);
  res.status(500).json({ error: "internal_error" });
});
2) GET /holidays?from=2026-04-01&to=2026-04-30 → 400 Bad Request
Meaning: your backend is rejecting the request as invalid, before it even tries to process normally.

Most likely validators:

It expects start/end not from/to

It expects ISO timestamps like 2026-04-01T00:00:00.000Z

It expects from <= to (yours is fine)

It expects dates in a different format (e.g. YYYY/MM/DD)

What to do
Find the backend route for /holidays and check what query params it reads.

If it’s expecting startDate/endDate, then fix frontend:

get("/holidays", { params: { startDate: from, endDate: to } })
Or if backend wants full timestamps:

const start = `${from}T00:00:00.000Z`;
const end = `${to}T23:59:59.999Z`;
3) GET /cleaner/holiday-overrides?from=...&to=... → 500
Meaning: same as (1): backend handler is crashing.

But notice the pattern:

/holidays returns 400 (validation / contract mismatch)

the cleaner-specific endpoints return 500 (runtime crash)

That screams: endpoint contract mismatch + missing/invalid auth context.

The real root cause (most probable) 🔥
Your Calendar page is calling holiday endpoints that your current backend doesn’t fully support (or expects different params / auth). So:

/holidays → validator says “bad query params” → 400

/cleaner/holiday-* → code assumes cleaner identity + DB tables exist → crashes → 500

Quick stabilizer (so UI stops exploding) ✅
If you want the app usable immediately, stub these endpoints to return empty data while you build the real models:

app.get("/cleaner/holiday-settings", (req, res) => {
  res.json({ timezone: "America/Los_Angeles", weeklyAvailability: [], blockedDates: [] });
});

app.get("/holidays", (req, res) => {
  res.json({ holidays: [] });
});

app.get("/cleaner/holiday-overrides", (req, res) => {
  res.json({ overrides: [] });
});
What I need from you to pinpoint the exact fix 🎯
Paste the backend console log stack trace for ONE of the 500s (holiday-settings or holiday-overrides). The frontend stack is noise; the backend stack will name the failing line instantly.
